# 一贯天机直讲

Alas! Is not the human heart inherently good? Yet what causes it to stray from goodness is but the coercion of circumstances and the pressures of the times. When the pursuit of fame and profit runs rampant, snares are already set and pitfalls laid—even the worthy can only soar high and far, concealing themselves beyond the dust of the world. Why is this? They refuse to drift with the current or ride the waves to violate the Dao, nor will they engage in scheming and contention to lose their true nature. By withdrawing from the world and transcending appearances, avoiding entanglement in words to escape the constraints of verbal explanation—is this not what is meant by the Great Dao of preserving authenticity?

What humans receive from Heaven is fundamentally an empty, luminous awareness, possessing all principles and responding to all affairs. Yet when enticed by the clamor of external things and obscured by the tumult of human desires, their bright virtue is thus dimmed. Hence, those deeply mired in cravings have shallow celestial potential, while those less swayed by worldly allure preserve their nature and life. This is why the worthy sages of orderly ages must cultivate indifference to fame and wealth to clarify their aspirations, and why the transcendent immortals and buddhas of otherworldly realms must embrace purity to return to the origin—is it not for this very reason?

Upon examining the three teachings of Confucianism, Daoism, and Buddhism, I find they share a common source, their essence lying in restraining anger, curbing desires, and mastering the self to return to propriety as the gateway to virtue. Thus, scriptures such as the *Yinfu Jing*, *Daode Jing*, and *Xinyin Jing*, along with works like the *Great Learning* and *Doctrine of the Mean*, all take self-cultivation, bright virtue, purity, and non-action as their foundation. They do not rely on figurative language, unlike other Daoist texts replete with metaphors—tortoises and snakes, dragons and tigers, lead and mercury, alchemical furnaces—obscure imagery that leaves readers bewildered, as if lost in a thick fog, even leading some to mistakenly believe in elixir consumption, talismans, bedroom arts, or alchemical refinement.

Surveying the literati and officials, many retreat into Chan monasteries in their later years to seek enlightenment of the mind and nature. Initially, they may have been drawn to the teachings of longevity and ascension, but finding the terminology and principles too abstruse, they turn instead to Chan’s simplicity and direct pointing. Thus, Buddhism flourishes while Daoism wanes, and the Great Dao grows ever more obscured.

Since my *jiazi* year in Jiaozhou, when I served as director, I have studied the teachings of the Complete Perfection school. However, burdened by official duties, I could not devote myself wholeheartedly, and my gains were meager. Recently, seeking refuge from the clamor of the old capital, I chanced upon the book *Direct Explications of the Celestial Mechanism of Unity* in a bookshop. Upon perusal, I learned it was compiled by the Perfected One Wei Zezhi of Western Shu, a recent lecture series delivered in Beijing during the *jiazi* year of the Republic. It meticulously annotates the essence of the three teachings and the profound meanings of various scriptures, exhaustively elucidating them—truly a rarity among Daoist texts through the ages. All the secret oral instructions for cultivating authenticity, along with the esoteric doctrines of the Mysterious School, Buddhist classics, and the mysteries of pre- and post-celestial realms, are clearly annotated, making everything plain at a glance. It serves as a golden needle and precious raft for those cultivating without a teacher. If one practices diligently according to its guidance, not only can one prolong life and enhance vitality, but even ascension to the immortal registers is attainable.

I had intended to publish it promptly to disseminate it widely and remedy the world’s decline. However, in the third volume, the commentary on the seventeenth chapter of the *Yinfu Jing* was missing a page, leaving the work incomplete. After searching for years, I could not locate it. Reluctantly, I left a blank space for this chapter and proceeded with publication. Most remarkably, the day before typesetting, Li Qunwenhao, an employee of the bookshop, happened upon a tattered third volume at a stall near Desheng Gate. Within it lay the missing commentary on the seventeenth chapter of the *Yinfu Jing*. I obtained it as if gaining a priceless treasure, immediately transcribed it into the original book, and sent it to the typesetter. Without the unseen protection of divine spirits, how could this have come to pass?

On the day preceding the Beginning of Winter in the year *xinsi* of the thirty-first year of the Republic (1941), respectfully inscribed by Gao Enhong of Ding’an, Penglai

**Preface II**

For over twenty years, I have revered the Great Dao of the Mysterious and True. Yet the alchemical classics and Daoist scriptures I have perused are replete with cryptic phrases and enigmatic expressions, rendering them exceedingly difficult to comprehend. Could it be that their authors, fearing transmission to the unworthy, deliberately employed manifold metaphors to veil their teachings from plain sight?

Master Gao Ding’an of Penglai has long devoted himself to the study of the Dao. In his daily cultivation of body and mind, he has profoundly grasped the *samādhi* of nurturing the True. Though nearing seventy in years, he appears no older than a man in his forties. The depth of his practice is truly exemplary.

His collection of ancient and modern Daoist texts includes many rare works. I have been fortunate to receive his repeated generosity in sharing them, from which I have greatly benefited. Among these, the *Direct Explication of the Celestial Mechanism of the One Unifying Principle* stands as the lodestar of modern Daoist literature. Alas, its original printing is blurred, and the book itself has become exceedingly scarce, making it difficult to acquire and study—an undeniable regret.

This work expounds the stages of practice with meticulous clarity, tracing each step to its source. Should Confucians encounter it, they may fathom principle and fulfill their nature to attain sageliness; Buddhists, they may illuminate the mind and perceive their nature to achieve buddhahood; Daoists, they may cultivate the True and nurture their nature to become immortals. If we but follow its guidance in practice, those in the world may receive the authentic transmission of sages and worthies, fulfilling the human Dao of self-cultivation, family regulation, state governance, and world pacification; those beyond the world may grasp the wondrous truths of immortals and buddhas, fulfilling the celestial Dao of emptiness and purity.

For the learning that unifies the Three Teachings—though their paths differ, their destination is the same—this volume encompasses the vast, profound, and subtle ultimate Dao in its entirety, serving as a compass for all who seek the Way.

In former years, Master Gao diligently served the nation, overseeing transportation and education, and his meritorious contributions to public welfare earned renown at home and abroad. Though he has since retired to a life of seclusion, his heart remains set on benefiting the world even in his leisure. Recently, he took up this work, meticulously proofread it, and generously funded its carving and printing to ensure its wide dissemination.

I know that once this book is broadly circulated, the Great Dao of the Mysterious and True will surely flourish day by day. The misguided may be corrected, the deluded may awaken, and none shall stray into heterodox paths or suffer harm. Its benefit to the world’s moral order and the human heart will be profound indeed.

Respectfully inscribed by Ye Yian, a later student, on the day of the Beginning of Winter in the year *xinsi*

**Opening of the *Direct Explication of the Celestial Mechanism of the One Unifying Principle***

The Dao has long been obscured: the worthy overshoot it, while the unworthy fall short. The Dao has long gone unenacted: the wise overshoot it, while the foolish fall short. Both overshooting and falling short deviate from the Mean.

The Great Dao resides precisely in the Mean—it is no lofty, unattainable endeavor. Thus Confucius was called the Sage of Timely Centrality, and the two books *The Great Learning* and *The Doctrine of the Mean* became the transmitted teachings of the Sage’s school, unchanging through the ages. Yet precisely because it is so ordinary, few truly understand it. Even sages as wise as Yan [Yuan] and Min [Sun] could not grasp its principles without a teacher. This is why the sages of the Three Teachings all used the character *zhong* (centrality) to represent it.

Centrality is the unchanging principle of the world. "Not deviating" is called *zhong*; "not altering" is called *yong*. As the *Book of Changes* says: *"Qian operates through simplicity in knowing; Kun operates through simplicity in functioning."* The words "simplicity" and "ease" are none other than the Mean. The Way of the Mean lies within the ordinary affairs of daily life. Thus it is said: *"The hundred clans use it daily yet do not know it."*

This Dao can be spoken of, yet it is not the constant Dao. It is the human Dao, and it is also the Heavenly Dao. Heaven attains it and becomes clear; Earth attains it and becomes tranquil; valleys attain it and become full; humans attain it and live long; kings and lords attain it to become the steadfast pillars of the world.

Laozi said: *"Attain the One, and all things are complete."* The One is singularity, supremacy, the Great One, the Supreme Ultimate. It is one and numinous, and as the unchanging source of all things, its generation of beings is unfathomable. Zengzi said: *"My Way is unified by the One."* For the One is the undivided image of the Two Modes, the primordial *qi* that gives birth to Heaven, Earth, humanity, and all things. In the Supreme Ultimate, it is the primordial *qi*; in Heaven, it is emptiness and numinosity; on Earth, it is the steadfast origin and the *qi* of life. When humans receive it, it becomes their nature and life—this is the Dao.

Follow it, and you fully receive and fully return to it; the Dao is within you. This is the highest virtue, the achievement of sudden perfection. As for lesser virtue, it must be cultivated. What is cultivation? It is the cultivation of the Way of nature and life. Since it is called cultivation, there must be methods and transmission—this is why it is called teaching, the gradual method.

In truth, Heaven and Earth cannot exist a single day without the Dao; without the Dao, Heaven and Earth would collapse. Humans cannot be separated from the Dao for even a moment; separated from the Dao, they cannot live. Yet worldly people, confined within the six senses and seven emotions, are so habituated to the Dao that they do not recognize it—just as fish swim daily in water yet do not know it as water.

Our nation established its teachings on the Dao. Confucianism and Daoism were originally one family, both without ritual forms. Only since the Qin and Han dynasties have distinctions arisen.

Thus, Confucians established their own robes and caps, while Zhang Zhengyi, the Celestial Master, further defined the vestments of the Daoist tradition. The *Han Shu: Yi Wen Zhi* further distinguished the teachings of Confucianism and Daoism, thereby forming the formal structures of religion. With the arrival of Buddhism in China, the term "Three Teachings" emerged. Thereafter, Confucians sank into philology and literary composition, Daoists fell into talismans and incantations, and Buddhists flowed into ritual fasts and sutra-chanting—obscuring the Great Dao entirely.

Later, Islam and Western Christianity entered, making Five Teachings in all. Examined impartially, their principles are fundamentally the same. Yet those within each tradition seek only in forms and appearances, utterly unaware of the "Doctrine of the Mean"—this is why the world is in chaos.

Now, at the extremity of decline, change arises, and through change comes understanding. In our nation, many turn to the gates of the Three Teachings to study the learning of nature and life. Yet some stray into heterodox schools, while others fall into external paths. Otherwise, they remain in the lower vehicle of sensory forms, chanting sutras, prostrating in repentance, or praying to the Dipper for blessings—far removed from the Dao, let alone the supreme vehicle, the highest and most transcendent Primordial Great Dao!

By the grace of Heaven, I have been fortunate to hear the wondrous truth from a true master and have studied the classics of the Three Teachings, gaining some insight. Not daring to keep this secret, I gather like-minded companions to discuss and elucidate the true principles of alchemical texts and Buddhist sutras, lest future generations be led astray.

Compared to past ritual codes, this may risk revealing celestial secrets. Yet in this age, great principles are perverted and subtle teachings lost—one cannot remain silent. Therefore, I have carefully arranged the stages of the "fire times" and disordered their sequence, slightly concealing their meaning to allow seekers to realize it for themselves.

May my fellow practitioners keep this secret in their cultivation and not transmit it carelessly. Moreover, this Dao must be verified through practice: those with keen wisdom may suddenly ascend to the highest realm, attaining sagehood at once, while those of duller faculties may gradually awaken to perfect enlightenment. How can this compare to those who merely form societies and gatherings to propagate the Dao?

*Inscribed by Houjue Daoren Wei Yao on the Winter Solstice of the Jiazi year*
*Direct Teachings of the Celestial Mechanism, Scroll One, First Lecture*

The Qian and Kun, Kan and Li serve as the bellows and hinge of Heaven and Earth, while the inner and outer voids turn the hub and true axle. The Eight Trigrams are divided into Prior Heaven and Posterior Heaven, and thus Qian and Kun must also be distinguished as Prior and Posterior. Prior Heaven is the essence, Posterior Heaven the function.

The so-called "Qian" and "Kun" are the one yin and one yang, born of the Supreme Ultimate. The Supreme Ultimate arises from the Ultimateless, and the Ultimateless is truly Non-Being. From the Ultimateless emerges the Supreme Ultimate, whose essence remains formless—its image is ○. When the Supreme Ultimate moves, it generates one qi, its image ⊙, still without form or appearance, invisible to sight and inaudible to hearing—this is the qi of the one yang.

When the formless qi is full, it gives rise to the formed qi, which is stillness generating yin. Thus, the formless qi, being pure and light, ascends to become Heaven, or Qian; the formed qi, being heavy and turbid, descends to congeal as Earth, or Kun. Their image is ☰, and the Two Modes are established. Above is Heaven, below is Earth, and between them lies the true void. Within this true void, there is still a Supreme Ultimate. Without qi or formed qi, combining the formless qi of Heaven and the formed qi of Earth, they become three. Three is one—its image is ☰—Heaven and Earth are separated by eighty-four thousand li. At the midpoint of twenty-four thousand li lies the true void, forming a Supreme Ultimate known as the "Great Central Ultimate," also called the "Heart of Heaven and Earth," abbreviated as the "Heavenly Heart" or "Dao Heart."

Once the Two Modes are divided, yin and yang interact, qi and formed qi intermingle, further dividing into the Four Images. Their image is ☲☵: yang envelops yin, with formless qi on the outside and formed qi within, becoming the sun; yin envelops yang, with formed qi on the outside and formless qi within, becoming the moon. Between Heaven, Earth, sun, and moon, there is still a center—the true void of the Supreme Ultimate. Combining Heaven, Earth, sun, and moon makes five; five is three, and three is one.

Guangchengzi taught the Yellow Emperor the Dao of Three-in-One, and *The Awakening to Reality* states, "Three, five, and one—these three words; rare are those who truly understand them through the ages," referring precisely to this. One is the Supreme Ultimate before Heaven and Earth divided; three is the Supreme Ultimate after Heaven and Earth divided; five is the Supreme Ultimate after the Four Images were established. The Supreme Ultimate envelops Heaven and Earth, and Heaven and Earth in turn envelop the Supreme Ultimate.

To illustrate with an object: consider a chicken egg, within which there is a small void of pale yellow, enveloped by yellow, which is further enveloped by white, while both ends of the egg have air pockets. Its image is as follows: the central void is the internally contained Supreme Ultimate, the white and yellow are Heaven and Earth, and the air pockets at the ends are the externally enveloping Supreme Ultimate. This is but one example; in truth, the generation and transformation of all things in Heaven and Earth share the same pattern as the great creation—all originate from the central void and are subsequently augmented from without. The embryos of animals and the seeds of plants are no exception. Thus can the divine marvel of creation be perceived.

Those who cultivate the Dao observe the great creation and take it as their model, returning from four to two, from two to one, from the substantial to the void, from Posterior Heaven to Prior Heaven—all beginning within this void, returning to the original Supreme Ultimate. The sages of the Three Teachings all use the character "middle" (中) to represent the Supreme Ultimate and describe this void essence. The essence of the Supreme Ultimate is ○; adding the line of principle and qi (丨) forms the character "middle" (中). "Middle" signifies emptiness, penetration; combining two "middles" forms the character "pervade" (貫). The ancient form of "pervade" appears as 毌. Within the cultivator’s body is one "middle," and outside the body is another "middle"; combining the two "middles" forms "pervade," as in "My Dao pervades all with one thread," and the Dao of the *Doctrine of the Mean* is attained.

Moreover, "middle" means correctness, the absence of bias. No material object can be unbiased and correct, for all are partial. Only the void is perfectly centered, unbiased, boundless without and infinitesimal within—thus can the essence of the Supreme Ultimate be perceived.

*The Seal of the Unity of the Three* states: "Qian and Kun are the gate and door of the Changes, the parents of all trigrams." Qian is yang, and the yang qi is formless—depicted by a single unbroken line (一) to represent it. Kun is yin, and the yin qi is formed—depicted by a broken line (一 一) to represent it. Accumulating three lines forms Qian ☰, which is Heaven; accumulating six lines forms Kun ☷, which is Earth. "Three generates the myriad things," and the character "three" (三) also implies completion, beginning and ending—thus trigrams are formed by accumulating three lines.

Qian and Kun interact to form Li and Kan; Heaven and Earth interact to form the sun and moon. Qian and Kun employ Li and Kan as their function; Heaven and Earth employ the sun and moon as their function. What is the "Change" (*Yi*)? It is precisely the sun and moon. Daoists call it the "elixir" (丹), combining "sun above" and "moon below" to form the character *dan*; Buddhists call it "brightness" (明), combining "sun on the left" and "moon on the right" to form the character *ming*; Confucians call it the "Change" (易), also combining "sun above" and "moon below" to form the character *yi*. Change, brightness, elixir—all are one.

The function of Heaven and Earth is manifested through daily use: the accumulation of their ascent and descent gives rise to cold and heat, dividing the four seasons. The transformation and generation of the myriad things all pass through the four seasons to achieve completion. The East is the qi of wood, corresponding to spring—wood possesses the virtue of generation, and the myriad things are born. The South is the qi of fire, corresponding to summer—fire possesses the ascending virtue, and the myriad things grow.

The West is the qi of metal, corresponding to autumn—metal possesses the power to kill, and the myriad things wither upon encountering it. The North is the qi of water, corresponding to winter—water is the qi of storage, and the myriad things lie concealed. These are the qi of the Five Phases in their primordial state.

This is attested in the ancient *Hetu* (*River Diagram*): two and seven are in front, one and six behind, three and eight to the left, four and nine to the right, and five and ten reside in the center. One and six represent the northern direction, *ren* and *gui* water; two and seven represent the southern direction, *bing* and *ding* fire; three and eight represent the eastern direction, *jia* and *yi* wood; four and nine represent the western direction, *geng* and *xin* metal; five and ten represent the central *wu* and *ji* earth. The central five symbolizes the Supreme Ultimate, containing the Four Images within its emptiness—formless yet inwardly enfolding wondrous being, and further symbolizing the Supreme Ultimate’s embrace of primordial qi.

Speaking of their initial transformations: the yang qi of Heaven One is by nature moist and quiescent, named water, and stored in the North. The North is the *kun* direction of completion and ending, thus symbolizing winter. Winter governs return and storage, serving as the root of the myriad things’ generation. The yin qi of Earth Two is by nature ascending and dynamic, named fire, and attached to the South. The South is the supremely honored *qian* direction, thus symbolizing summer. Summer governs growth and nourishment, the time when the myriad images intermingle in brightness.

The East Three combines the qi of Heaven One and Earth Two to form its nature, governing generation, its qi warm—thus symbolizing spring, mild and possessing the virtue of benevolence. The West Four combines the qi of two waters and one fire, its nature governing killing, its qi cool—thus symbolizing autumn, stern and possessing the virtue of righteousness and resolve. Qi that is stirred and surging becomes wind; thus, the winds of East, South, West, and North each follow their nature, and generation, growth, killing, and storage perfectly accord with their virtues.

Metal, wood, water, and fire occupy the four directions, while the space between them is named five, the qi of earth. Earth flourishes in all four seasons, concealed within metal, wood, water, and fire. The myriad things are born from emptiness, established through emptiness—there is nothing that does not contain emptiness within. Thus, the qi of earth circulates through the Four Images, present everywhere. These are the Five Phases of primordial qi transformation. On earth, they manifest as the five forms of water, fire, wood, metal, and earth; in humans, they correspond to the five constants of benevolence, righteousness, propriety, wisdom, and trustworthiness.

Benevolence arises from nature, sincerity within manifesting without—like the East Three’s generative qi. Righteousness arises from emotion, external stimuli resonating within—like the West Four’s stern and resolute qi. Propriety is born of the heart, outwardly expressed as refinement—like the South Two’s fire. Wisdom emerges from the body, inwardly containing ingenuity—like the North One’s water. Trustworthiness responds from the central palace, the wondrous being of the central palace—benevolence, righteousness, propriety, and wisdom all depend on trustworthiness to be realized. Trustworthiness is the foundation of human integrity, like the central earth flourishing in all four seasons. Thus, true intention is called true earth, the true sovereign of both nature and life in dual cultivation.

Why is it named the "gate and door"? The cosmos may be likened to a chamber: *qian* and *kun* extend its doorframe, while the sun and moon pass through it in their movements—such is its image. The generation and transformation of the myriad things arise from the Five Phases; the waxing and waning of the Five Phases arise from the sun and moon. One ascent and one descent divide day and night; one departure and one return complete cold and heat.

Today, as the time coincides with the Winter Solstice, it is precisely the day when the sun and moon exchange their light. The sun and moon intersect north and south: the sun above, the moon below, the moon absorbing the sun’s light, and the first yang is born. From one yang to two yang, then three yang—when abundance peaks, decline follows. When the time coincides with the Summer Solstice, the sun and moon intersect east and west: the sun absorbs the moon’s qi, and yin is born. From one yin to two yin, then three yin—when yin wanes, yang returns. Again, the Winter Solstice arrives, and the sun completes one circuit of the heavens, requiring one year. As for the moon’s movement, it completes one circuit each month.

All these movements of the sun and moon are the waxing and waning of the yin and yang qi, opening and closing without fail—this is why it is called the gate and door. *Qian* and *kun* are also the "parents of all hexagrams": *qian* is the ancestor of all yang, the father; *kun* is the ancestor of all yin, the mother. Father and mother unite, yin and yang intersect, giving birth to sons and daughters. *Qian* seeks once from *kun*, obtaining its first line, and *xun* is born, the eldest daughter. *Kun* seeks once from *qian*, obtaining its first line, and *zhen* is born, the eldest son. A second seeking produces *li* and *kan*, the middle daughter and middle son; a third seeking produces *dui* and *gen*, the youngest daughter and youngest son—thus, three daughters and three sons, as explained by the line counts.

At the initial intersection of *qian* and *kun* qi, *kan* and *li* are born first, followed by *gen* and *dui*, and finally *zhen* and *xun*. After the six children are born, *qian* and *kun* grow old, retiring to the northwest and southwest, allowing the middle son and middle daughter to assume their proper roles and heed their commands. Thus it is said: "*Qian* and *kun* are the body; *kan* and *li* are the function." *Li* is yang without and yin within—the sun; *kan* is yin without and yang within—the moon. After Heaven and Earth are established in their positions, they open their gate and door, allowing the sun and moon to move and complete creation—this is the meaning of "function."

From the doubling of the eight trigrams arise the sixty-four hexagrams and three hundred eighty-four lines. Tracing the flow to explore the source, examining the end to fathom the root—all emerge from the two hexagrams *qian* and *kun*, the two lines of one yin and one yang.

Thus it is said: "*Qian* and *kun* are the parents of all hexagrams."

Now, considering *qian*, *kun*, *li*, and *kan* as they manifest in the human body: *qian*-Heaven is *xing* (nature), *kun*-Earth is *ming* (destiny). *Xing* is the root of nature, *ming* the stem of destiny. *Li* is the acquired *xing*, *kan* the acquired *ming*. The first chapter of the *Huangting Jing* states:

> Above dwells the hun-spirit, below the Gate of Origin;
> Left is Lesser Yang, right Greater Yin.
> Behind lies the Secret Door, before the Gate of Life—
> Exhaling moon, inhaling sun, breath abides therein.

These six—above, below, front, back, left, and right—implicitly contain a central point, which is emptiness. The Great Emptiness takes Heaven and Earth as its true womb, the sun and moon as its true breath. The rising and setting of the sun and moon are the exhalation and inhalation of the Great Emptiness. Likewise, the breath within the human body mirrors the Great Emptiness, its egress and ingress refined by a sun and moon—also named *kan* and *li*. These *kan* and *li* are the acquired *xing* and *ming*.

The gates of *qian* and *kun* in the human body correspond to above and below. In the Dao of the Elixir, *qian* is also called the crucible, and *kun* the furnace, with the Great Emptiness as the *qian*-crucible and the Great Ultimate as the *kun*-furnace. The emptiness within the human body is the Great Emptiness; the empty apertures within the human body are the Great Ultimate. Thus, the eight gates and nine apertures are all portals of the human body—all are the Great Ultimate.

The *Daode Jing* states: "Abide in non-desire to observe its mysteries; abide in desire to observe its apertures." The mysteries are the Great Emptiness; the apertures are the Great Ultimate. The method of observation lies in stilling all thoughts to observe the mysteries and focusing the mind unwaveringly to observe the apertures. The "non-desire" and "desire" refer to "stilling all thoughts" and "focusing the mind unwaveringly," not the presence or absence of worldly desires.

When the scholar enters seclusion, spirit and *qi* intermingle, merging into oneness. Over time, they return to primordial chaos, entering the realm of nothingness. This is the state of no thought arising, wherein one may observe the mysteries. Yet the active mind is stilled, not the illuminating mind—wisdom remains yet is not employed, awareness persists within non-awareness, naturally and without contrivance, the luminous essence shining forth. This is the state of unwavering focus, wherein one may observe the apertures.

The wondrous aperture within the human body is the Mysterious Pass—the most profound and wondrous mechanism between Heaven and Earth. The vast emptiness of Heaven and Earth and the small emptiness of the human body communicate ceaselessly through these gates. Their configuration is as follows:

Here, the scholar establishes the furnace and crucible, each with its own sequence. First, turning the light inward and observing within, from movement to stillness, until stillness is perfected and the Great Ultimate furnace is founded. Next, entering the primordial chaos, returning to emptiness, until emptiness is absolute and the Great Emptiness crucible manifests—thus is the work of establishing furnace and crucible complete.

Wu Chongxu said: "The crucible is no crucible; the furnace is no jade furnace." Crucible and furnace are originally formless, yet from ancient times to the present, how many have erred in their understanding of these two! Here, I reveal their truth—those with discerning eyes will know where to begin.

In the Primordial Eight Trigrams, *qian* is south and *kun* north, *li* east and *kan* west. South above and north below, Heaven and Earth assume their positions; east left and west right, the sun and moon move in their courses. Yin and yang maintain their constancy, hardness and softness correspond, and creation is accomplished. The *qian*-origin initiates, *qian* faces south and acts not; the *kun*-origin engenders, quietly following and upholding Heaven’s virtue. The sun rises in the east, the moon sets in the west, revolving and turning to generate the images of creation.

Heaven and Earth act not, yet the sun and moon act; the sage observes the sun and moon’s movements and knows the waxing and waning of Heaven and Earth. Confucius said: "What does Heaven say? The four seasons proceed, and the hundred creatures are born." Thus, the generative transformation of Heaven and Earth is unseen, while the revolving wheel of the sun and moon is visible. This is why in the Acquired Eight Trigrams, *kan* and *li* occupy the proper positions of south and north, while *qian* and *kun* are relegated to disuse—this is the Dao of Heaven and Earth as body, the sun and moon as function.

The *Cantong Qi* states: "*Kan* and *li* frame the void, turning the hub and axle. The four trigrams of the female and male serve as bellows and pipes." This speaks of the function of the sun and moon. The gates of Heaven and Earth remain unmoving, while the sun and moon revolve within the emptiness. A single *qi* circulates: in the small, through day and night, waxing and waning; in the greater, through spring and autumn, cold and heat; in the greatest, through cosmic eras and kalpas, spanning ten thousand eons without losing its order. Waxing and waning, growth and decline arise purely of themselves, without a ruler—yet the emptiness truly governs, hence it is called "numinous emptiness," commonly likened to a bellows.

The pipe is the empty box; the bellows, the device that draws and pushes air within. One draw and *qi* issues forth; one push and *qi* enters. One exhalation, one inhalation, and the *qi* fans the fire. When exhalation and inhalation are harmonized, the fire in the furnace blazes upward, neither scorching nor extinguishing. The smith relies on this fire to refine metal.

The sun and moon in space are the breath of Heaven and Earth, their *qi*-mechanism rising and falling naturally in balance—are they not the bellows and pipes? They are the emptiness between Heaven and Earth. The circulation of *qi* occurs within this emptiness.

The flourishing and withering of the myriad things likewise occur within this emptiness. Is it not the power of this emptiness that harmonizes this measure? Above the heavens and below the earth, the sun rises in the east and the moon sets in the west—up and down are like gates, left and right are like the encompassing frame. Are they not the bellows and pipes of the smith? And the sun and moon in their courses, with each waning and each breath, are they not the bellows and pipes opening and closing freely? Thus it is said: *"Empty yet never full, in motion it ever produces."*

Heaven and Earth establish the positions of high and low; Kan and Li array the left and right frames. The four trigrams, one female and one male, provide the resources for generation and inception, establishing the foundation of the myriad transformations. Wei Boyang’s *"encompassing frame"* describes the workings of creation within the emptiness—its profundity is most wondrous.

The human body is a small heaven and earth. At the moment of receiving *qi*, it responds to the Great Emptiness and is endowed with nature—this is *"forming images in heaven."* Through the Supreme Ultimate, it establishes destiny—this is *"forming shapes on earth."* Once the bodily form is complete, it emerges with the sun and enters with the moon, using them for breath. The sun and moon in their courses complete one revolution of 365 degrees, while the rising and falling of yin and yang occur 135,000 times. The breaths of all living people in a day and night likewise number 13,500. The sun and moon’s progression makes one revolution in a year; a person’s breathing makes one revolution in a day and night. The twenty-four solar terms and seventy-two seasonal markers correspond to the meridians and joints of the human body, to the breaths of exhalation and inhalation, and at all times communicate with the Great Emptiness of heaven and earth. Qian and Kun, Kan and Li are already complete within the human body. To know why gates and frames are gates and frames is to find the Dao within them.

*The Canticle* further states: *"Covering and veiling the Dao of yin and yang is like a craftsman driving a chariot—following the inked line, holding the reins and bit, aligning the compass and square, tracking the wheel-ruts, abiding in the center to govern the exterior. The reckoning lies in the pitch-pipes and calendar."* This elaborates on the waxing and waning of the one yin and one yang, the functions of the Kan and Li *qi*. The covering descent and veiling ascent correspond to the hexagrams *Fu* and *Gou*, and are verified in the twenty-four solar terms and seventy-two seasonal markers. Thus Confucius said: *"In* Fu *is seen the heart of heaven and earth!"* (See *The Book of Changes*, *Fu* hexagram.) And in the *Qian* hexagram’s nine in the third place, he said: *"All day long* Qian *is* Qian*, returning and repeating the Dao."* For this is verified in the movement and stillness of the *qi*-mechanism, extended even to a full year. The rise of calendrical reckoning takes its model from this.

The metaphor of *"driving"* comes from Laozi’s *"Thirty spokes share one hub"*—the hub is the empty cavity of the revolving axle. The cart moves by its wheels, the wheels are threaded by the axle, and what enables the axle to thread them as one is the emptiness at the hub’s center. Without this emptiness, the cart cannot move. Even with wheel-ruts, what use are they? *The Canticle* takes the axle as the norm, while the operation lies in the hub, hence it says *"abiding in the center to govern the exterior."* This is like the sun and moon revolving within the emptiness to complete the four seasons.

All things have a center; the center is the norm, meaning it is without bias. Among tangible things, none is so centered as to be without bias. Only the emptiness within things is unbiased, without exterior. Great as the empty valleys of heaven and earth, small as the hollow receptacles of the myriad things—all are centers. And within this emptiness, the ten thousand beings are truly conceived. The sages of the Three Teachings all speak of the center. The cauldron of the Great Emptiness is the center; the furnace of the Supreme Ultimate is also the center. The human center communicates with the center of heaven and earth, thus one can steal the spirit-*qi* of heaven and earth to make it one’s own spirit-*qi*. The center of heaven, earth, and the myriad things communicates with the human center, thus it can steal the human spirit-*qi* and subject it to birth, aging, sickness, and death.

Each person possesses one Supreme Ultimate; each of the myriad things likewise possesses one Supreme Ultimate. If one nurtures it well, a person can stand in the position of heaven and earth, nourish the myriad things, extend it to fill the six directions, or roll it up and withdraw it into secrecy. Thus Mencius said: *"The ten thousand things are all complete within me!"* (See *Mencius*, *"Exhausting the Mind," Part One*.) The Supreme Ultimate is one and numinous. Zisi said: *"As a thing, it is not two, thus its generation of things is unfathomable."* (See *The Doctrine of the Mean*.) What, then, is this thing whose generation is unfathomable? It is the Supreme Ultimate, solitary and without peer.

The Supreme Ultimate generates the Two Modes; the Two Modes are yin and yang, *qi* and breath. From the Two Modes, transformation proceeds—from the Two Modes to the Four Images and Eight Trigrams, and on to the myriad billions, all are called *"numbers."* Numbers fundamentally begin with the opposition of yin and yang. When heaven and earth divide, numbers arise. Thus *The Book of Changes* says: *"Three for heaven, two for earth, and the numbers are established."* The sun and moon in their courses, for a thousand autumns and ten thousand eons, do not deviate from their sequence. The two *qi* of yin and yang, in their waxing and waning, do not miss their seasonal markers. This is because numbers constrain them—hence the reckoning of calendars and pitch-pipes.

Only the prior-heaven Supreme Ultimate transcends numbers and is the beginning of heaven and earth. The posterior-heaven Supreme Ultimate (the center of heaven and earth) likewise transcends numbers and is the mother of the myriad things. The *"named"* Supreme Ultimate returns to the *"nameless"* Supreme Ultimate—this is called *"embracing simplicity and returning to the real,"* this is called *"returning to the root and recovering destiny."* This is why the Dao is the Dao, and why the wondrous apertures are cultivated in tandem.

The *Alchemical Classics* say: *"Where Qian and Kun unite is the true center."* *The Four Hundred Words on the Golden Elixir* says: *"This aperture is no ordinary aperture—it is formed by the union of Qian and Kun."*

The *"Spirit-Qi Cavern"* is named thus, for within it lies the essence of Kan and Li. Bai Yuchan said: *"The Mysterious Pass is the true center."* This so-called *"Mysterious Pass"* is yin-yang, the crucible and furnace—it is also the Great Void and the Supreme Ultimate of the prior diagram. Where the Mysterious Female unites, there lies the true center, there lies the Mysterious Pass.

*Laozi* says: *"The Dao that can be spoken is not the eternal Dao; the name that can be named is not the eternal name. The nameless is the beginning of heaven and earth; the named is the mother of the myriad things. Thus, constantly free from desire, one observes its mystery; constantly possessing desire, one observes its manifestations. These two emerge together yet differ in name—they are called the Mysterious. Mysterious and again mysterious, the gateway to all wonders."* Such is the case.

As creation shifts and transforms, it never loses its center. Wondrous being and true emptiness originally stem from one gate. The gate and its encompassing frame establish its wholeness; the empty valley’s transformative generation unfolds its function. How vast is the meaning of the Supreme Ultimate!

**Second Lecture: Cultivating Nature to Prolong Life and Postpone the Appointed Term**
**Receiving Qi at Birth Establishes the Foundation of the Dao**

Those who cultivate the Dao set up the furnace and establish the crucible to refine the true sun and moon. The sun and moon are Kan and Li; when Kan and Li merge, the elixir is formed; when Qian and Kun unite, the Great Elixir is achieved. First, refine essence into qi; next, refine qi into spirit; finally, refine spirit to return to emptiness—this is the return from the Supreme Ultimate to the Ultimateless.

The external medicine completes destiny and returns to the Supreme Ultimate; the internal medicine completes nature and returns to the Ultimateless. *The Canticle* says: *"To cultivate nature, prolong life, and postpone the appointed term."* Prolonging life requires seeking the treasure of destiny; cultivating nature restores its numinous emptiness.

For the human form, the prior-heaven transforms into the posterior-heaven—Qian and Kun transform into Kan and Li. Qian’s single yang sinks into Kan, and Kan’s single yang becomes *"Qian Metal,"* which is also the *"treasure of destiny."* *"Drawing from Kan to fill Li"* means extracting this treasure of destiny from Kan and returning it to Li. Li’s single yin then reverts to Kan’s middle line, restoring the original body of Qian and Kun, and the work of destiny is complete.

To clarify this principle, one must first explain the sequence of creation’s generation and the order of human conception and birth. Here is a detailed account:

Creation proceeds from the Supreme Ultimate to the Great Initial, from the Great Initial to the Great Commencement, from the Great Commencement to the Great Simplicity, and from the Great Simplicity to the Great Prime. The Great Commencement is the beginning of qi; the Great Simplicity is the beginning of form; the Great Prime is the beginning of substance.

Image is light, light pertains to fire, and the beginning of image is yang fire. Qi contains moisture, moisture is the beginning of water-qi, which is yin water. With a tangible body that changes over time, it becomes the root of ceaseless generation—thus, the beginning of form is wood. With a solid body that does not change, it becomes firm and unyielding metal—thus, the beginning of substance is metal. With these four—fire, water, wood, and metal—the Five Phases are established, their origin a single undifferentiated Supreme Ultimate.

The Supreme Ultimate’s true emptiness gives rise to wondrous being, and thus the foundation of heaven and earth is laid. Master Tan said: *"Kneading emptiness into clods, one sees the clods but not the emptiness; crushing clods into emptiness, one sees the emptiness but not the clods."* True emptiness and wondrous being emerge together yet differ in name. Within the center is the One, and within the One is the center. This is why it is called the Supreme Ultimate.

The beginning of human life follows the same pattern. From nothing comes being, from the Supreme Ultimate arise the Five Phases, and the embryo takes shape, limbs form—all in accord with the workings of cosmic creation. Before birth, nothing exists; this is the utmost emptiness, the Ultimateless. Daoist scriptures and Buddhist texts speak of *"the original face before parents were born"*—this is precisely it. The *"original face at the time of parents’ birth"* is the Supreme Ultimate.

For when a person is first conceived, the union of the father’s and mother’s essences stirs the prior-heaven qi, which comes from the formless and forms the embryo. At the moment of union, as desire stirs, the physical bodies unite, gradually leading to the union of their spirits. Through the action of their limbs, pleasure arises, and when pleasure reaches its peak, the minds of both man and woman become empty and hollow—even pleasure itself is unperceived, achieving true emptiness. The tangible act of union transforms into the intangible image of pure Kun. Kun is true yin, and only true yin can summon true yang. Thus, it stirs the prior-heaven qi within the Supreme Ultimate, circulating through the six directions, generating being from nothing. A single point of true yang, riding the emptiness, enters the mother’s womb, beginning the gestation. This point of true yang is the heavenly nature of destiny. In heaven, it is nature; in humans, when received at the start of gestation, it is called destiny.

For when man and woman, through pleasure, empty their bodies and minds, they first achieve the Ultimateless. Then, as their spirits and qi merge into one, they become a chaotic Supreme Ultimate, and true emptiness gives rise to a point of wondrous being—principle and qi. From the perspective of the Supreme Ultimate, this is *"being born from nothing"*; from the perspective of the human body, it is *"resonance in response to summoning."* This qi is originally empty, becoming the first qi a person receives—thus, it is called the *"prior-heaven of prior-heaven Qian’s true nature."*

Yet when this qi emerges from the formless, the spirits of the man and woman have already merged into an intangible whole. This point of yang qi enters within, resembling the image of (甲)○. The inner empty circle is this qi’s outer emptiness, symbolizing the union of spirits.

Once the spirits have merged, the breaths of the man and woman also intermingle, producing a tangible sphere of qi, resembling the image of (乙)○, concealed between the yin heel vessels. The (甲) image, drawn by the (乙) image, then enters and unites within it, forming the image of (丙)　, which follows the breath into the womb. This qi is the true mandate of Kun’s primordial power, thus called the *"prior-heaven within posterior-heaven."*

When united as (丙), nature and mandate become one, and only then do the father’s essence and mother’s blood envelop it externally, forming the primal embryo. Together, these constitute five layers of creation, which, when distinguished, are the Supreme Ultimate, the Great Beginning, the Great Inception, the Great Simplicity, and the Great Pristine. As depicted in the (丁) image:

- **甲** is the *"prior-heaven’s singular qi"*—Qian’s true nature—*"prior-heaven of prior-heaven."*
- **乙** is the *"harmony of the parents’ spirits and emotions"*—the nature of qi and material—*"prior-heaven."*
- **丙** is the *"qi born from the parents’ Kan and Li congealment"*—Kun’s true mandate—*"prior-heaven within posterior-heaven."*
- **丁** is the *"father’s essence"*—posterior-heaven.
- **戊** is the *"mother’s blood"*—posterior-heaven.

*(Note: The dashed lines represent emptiness, forming three encompassing layers that numerically align with the Five Phases.)*

The *Book of Changes* states: *"In heaven, it forms images; on earth, it takes shape."* (See *Xici I.*) Following the Dao to generate human life likewise accords with the creative workings of heaven and earth. **甲** and **乙** are both prior-heaven, possessing only images and thus derived from heaven; **丙** and **丁** are posterior-heaven, possessing form and substance and thus derived from earth.

Once the primal embryo is established, that which is received from heaven governs movement and stillness, while that received from earth clings to the prior-heaven to transform the physical form. When the Dao of the formless and the formed is complete, it renews day by day and month by month, gradually accumulating into the five viscera, six bowels, hundred bones, and nine palaces, forming the entire body.

After the placenta is fully formed, the umbilical cord connects to the mother’s breath, serving as the fetus’s respiration and absorbing external qi—this is posterior-heaven qi. This posterior-heaven qi enters the abdomen, lingering with the prior-heaven qi and the prior-heaven within posterior-heaven qi, *"forming images in heaven"*; it nourishes the prior-heaven within posterior-heaven qi and the posterior-heaven qi, *"taking shape on earth,"* silently fostering growth and developing the fetus. Such is the sequential process of human formation and embryonic structuring within the womb.

When the posterior-heaven qi is sufficient and the ten-month gestation is complete, movement reaches its extreme. At this extremity, it becomes exhausted; exhaustion gives rise to spiritual transformation, transformation leads to change, and suddenly, awareness emerges. Breaking through the placenta, the child is born—this occurs because the intermediate existence enters to take dominion, and the spirit and qi are now complete.

What is this intermediate existence? Commonly called the *"soul,"* in Daoism it is termed *"original essence,"* said to carry emotions and consciousness, also called *"conscious nature."* In Buddhism, it is called *"intermediate existence"* (Skt. *antarābhava*), said to bear the karmic roots from beginningless kalpas. Confucianism names it the *"human heart,"* containing the nature of food and desire. When it attaches to the human body, it becomes the spirit-soul; when it mingles with worldly emotions, it becomes the consciousness-spirit; when it drifts in emptiness, it is the intermediate existence. The *Śūraṅgama Sūtra* translates it as *"intermediate existence,"* perhaps because it is a purely yin, formless, and empty entity. Commonly, it is simply called the *"soul,"* though this is not entirely accurate. For *"soul"* is spoken of in contrast to *"corporeal soul"*—only when this entity enters the human body does the clear and numinous become the soul, while the turbid and coarse become the corporeal soul. At this stage, without a corporeal soul, how can there be a soul?

Moreover, Confucian texts say that when a person dies, the soul returns to heaven and the corporeal soul returns to earth, seemingly equating the soul with nature. There is also the saying of the *"three souls,"* which appears to refer to: one as the indestructible nature, another as this destructible intermediate existence, and a third as the ghostly soul that receives karmic retribution in hell. Later writers, carelessly blending the terminology of the Three Teachings, have made distinctions difficult to clarify, and as it is irrelevant to the Dao, there is no need to explain further.

Human heavenly nature is fundamentally empty and originally without birth or death. Daoism says, *"Each person is complete, each is perfectly realized"*; the *Heart Sūtra* states, *"Neither born nor destroyed, neither defiled nor pure, neither increasing nor decreasing"*; Confucianism calls it *"the Dao-heart, only subtle"*—all refer to this.

Yet the conscious nature is subject to birth and death. Thus, Buddhism takes *"transforming consciousness into wisdom"* as the Dao, while the Mysterious School takes *"refining the soul and corporeal soul, transmuting the consciousness-spirit"* as the Dao. The intermediate existence’s cycle of rebirth appears indestructible only because it carries the karmic roots and emotional consciousness from past kalpas. Without this, a person would perish at death—how could they be reborn?

The *Śūraṅgama Sūtra* states: *"The intermediate existence, without a master, drifts in emptiness and, drawn by the fetus’s resonance, attaches to the human body."* The *Clarifying the Obscure in the Kinship of the Three* says: *"When the ten-month gestation is complete, from within pure chaos and emptiness, a point of original essence emerges, entering my central palace of the spirit to become my master."* Thus, the text says: *"The body one receives is fundamentally empty. The original essence spreads like clouds, relying on qi to take its first form."*

For when a man and woman unite in essence, they receive the prior-heaven’s singular, empty qi to begin the embryo. Upon birth, they again receive the posterior-heaven’s numinous, empty qi to become a person. When the ten months are fulfilled, the posterior-heaven qi transmitted through the umbilical cord fills the fetal body, stirring the true emptiness. Within the stillness of the central palace, it suddenly resonates—this is the pure yang summoning its kindred pure yin. This pure yin intermediate existence, drifting in emptiness, upon receiving this resonance, is drawn like a magnet to iron or two electric charges attracting each other. In an instant, it attaches to the fetal body, entering directly into the central yellow spirit-chamber to become the master of this body.

Once the intermediate existence of pure yin enters, awareness immediately arises. This awareness governs qi and blood, extending to the limbs, and the hands and feet begin to move—just as one stretches upon waking from a deep dream, or like a boulder tumbling from a mountain, startling into sudden motion. At once, the hands part, the feet kick free of the fetal sac, and with the feet now unsupported, the body loses its balance, flipping head over heels to breach the birth canal. Thus the head emerges first, called "inversion at birth."

Yet while the fetus’s awareness arises from the attachment of the intermediate existence, that existence itself does not fully awaken upon entering the body. When drifting in emptiness, it remains in a state of undifferentiated chaos; without the intermediate existence, the fetus too remains unknowing. Only when the intermediate existence relies upon the body, uniting with the prior-heaven qi within posterior-heaven qi, does awareness awaken. And only when stirred by the breath of posterior-heaven qi does this awareness become functional. The three—intermediate existence, prior-heaven qi, and posterior-heaven qi—must converge to achieve animation; separated, they revert to nothingness. Thus, when a person nears death, the primordial qi (the *bing* qi) within the body is exhausted, and posterior-heaven breath ceases. With breath severed, the intermediate existence departs the corporeal shell, drifting away without trace. Daoist texts state, "A person does not die until the last fraction of yang qi is spent"—this is the principle.

The above describes events in the fetal body, while within it, the inner nature and life-force separate at this moment. To elaborate: at conception, the prior-heaven *qi* of *Qian*’s origin constitutes one’s nature, while the prior-heaven *qi* of *Kun*’s origin within posterior-heaven forms one’s life-force. As shown in the earlier diagram, nature and life-force, originally merged, jointly govern the formless creation, bound together by the breath transmitted through the umbilical cord, thus coalescing without dispersion. They further employ the father’s essence and mother’s blood to transform into the corporeal limbs, completing their formation by the seventh month. At completion, the fetus sits within the womb, legs folded with heels touching, pressing tightly against the "Yin Heel" aperture. As Zhang Ziyang’s *Eight Vessel Classic* states: "The Yin Heel vessel lies below the scrotum, above the anus, precisely in the *Xun* trigram’s domain between the thighs." The feet correspond to the *Zhen* trigram, and *Zhen* and *Xun* together form the union of eldest son and eldest daughter. The fetus’s hands clasp each other, sealing the apertures of nose and mouth, preventing breath through them and necessitating respiration via the navel. This is why the hands serve as the "gate of total retention," the human barrier. The hands correspond to the *Gen* trigram, and the mouth to *Dui*, forming the union of youngest son and youngest daughter. The eyes do not gaze outward, the ears do not hear outward—this mirrors the union of middle son and middle daughter within *Kan* and *Li*. The navel’s opening and closing, with qi ascending to the crown, and the crown’s rising and falling, embody the union of *Qian* and *Kun*, yin and yang. Such is the harmonious alignment of the prior-heaven eight trigrams, described here in external terms.

As for the internal, the nature of *Qian* and the life-force of *Kun* reside together in the central palace, merging into the Supreme Polarity’s form. By the tenth month, posterior-heaven qi is full, stirring the central palace, and from the void of the Supreme Polarity, existence arises—stimulated, it connects. The Supreme Polarity is one, posterior-heaven qi is two. One *qi* and two *qi* blend into a misty union, generating the third and producing primordial essence, splitting the primordial chaos. Though the intermediate existence enters from without, its attachment is a response; from the Supreme Polarity’s perspective, it is birth—such is the principle. As the intermediate existence enters, drawn by the misty union of the two *qi*, it is absorbed directly into the central palace, relying upon the midst of the three *qi*, and thus gains awareness. With this awareness’s first stir, heaven and earth invert, and the central palace—where my nature and life-force unite—is jolted awake, as if clouds parting to reveal the sun, suddenly radiant. Clear qi ascends, and the nature of *Qian*’s primordial yang *qi* is driven to the crown, entering the empty valley of the *Niwan* palace; turbid qi descends, and the life-force of *Kun*’s true *qi* settles into the empty cavity of the Life Gate between the kidneys, splitting the Supreme Polarity into the Two Modes.

Thereafter, the intermediate existence, a strong guest seizing the host’s place, occupies the spirit-chamber as its master—just as after heaven and earth split, the void between them becomes the repository for the generation of the myriad things. In symbolic terms, the intermediate existence, born of the union of *Qian* and *Kun*, is naturally the child of nature and life-force, and as the child inherits the father’s body, it assumes governance. Yet the intermediate existence inherently carries emotion and perception, along with the karmic roots of past lives, opening my six senses and entangling my nature and life-force—thus becoming a thief. Hence both Buddhist and Daoist traditions employ the metaphor of "mistaking the thief for one’s child."

Once the intermediate existence becomes the master of the posterior-heaven form, awareness functions through qi, and qi moves through awareness, cycling in mutual activation, opening the six gates. Yet at the moment of its first stir, birth occurs. Within the womb, the fetus shares the mother’s breath. Upon emerging, the hands part, revealing the apertures for respiration. The true yang of *Qian*’s origin resides in the Celestial Valley, and with yang summoning yin, posterior-heaven air rushes in through the nose, first filling the mouth—hence the newborn’s first cry. The umbilical cord is severed, and the true *qi* of *Kun*’s origin retreats into the Life Gate, deeply concealed. The fetal breath below the navel ceases, unable to sustain itself, and thus the infant suddenly feels hunger and can eat.

From this point onward, with every inhalation and exhalation, the intermediate existence lingers, further awakening awareness. With every sip and bite, the physical form is nourished, yet innate wisdom is obscured. The milk and water of the human world are laden with worldly passions; the consciousness of discriminating mind takes control, and the Dao-heart gradually dims. Thus, there are those in the world who can speak at birth and recall past causes, yet after drinking milk, all becomes vague. The common saying of "the soup of forgetfulness" refers precisely to the milk and water of this world. At birth, there is none who does not retain some knowledge of past lives. This is why moments of "sincere foreknowledge" often occur after severing ties with worldly sustenance.

Moreover, the intermediate existence enters and resides in the Central Palace, where it is numinous and aware, serving as the master within. The precelestial Five Agents within the body are thereby established, their configuration as follows:

These five are all formless, hence precelestial. Their distinction lies in the interplay of movement and stillness: Original Nature is the primordial ancestral nature; when still, it is fundamentally an empty body, yet when moved, it becomes numinous and is called Original Spirit. Original Emotion is inherited from the parents at conception, transformed and united with the intermediate existence to form it; thus, when still, it is the fundamental substance, and when moved, it is termed Original Essence. As for Original Qi, it is the root of human life; Original Nature, Original Spirit, and Original Essence all depend on Original Qi to move, making it the true master of the precelestial, residing at the center to govern all.

Humans possess two aspects: *hun* and *po*. The *hun* is the shadow of spirit and qi; when still, it is formless, yet when moved, it takes shape. The *po* is the surplus of essence and qi; when still, it has form, and when moved, it acquires substance. The *hun* is pure and favors stillness; in stillness, it connects with the numinous. The *po* is turbid and favors movement; in movement, it indulges in desire. Thus, there is the division of yang-*hun* and yin-*po*, both manipulated by the discriminating mind. After death, the *hun* scatters to repay past karmic debts, while the *po* remains to guard the corpse. As the Buddhist scriptures say, "Those who enjoy offerings and harm people are all the work of the *po*."

When the intermediate existence enters the womb, the fetal sac becomes numinous and aware—without entering the womb, the intermediate existence lacks spirit, and without uniting with the intermediate existence, the fetal sac remains inert. The transformations of the posterior-heaven depend on the intermediate existence, which in turn relies on posterior-heaven qi as its support; only upon union can movement occur. This is the Original Emotion of the fetus, which, when moved, descends to earth, letting out a sudden wail. The Primordial Chaos is split open, and the infant’s sorrowful cries cease not. As *The Collection of Central Harmony* states, "A single sword cleaves the chaos; two hands rend the Primordial Void."

From this point onward, the discriminating mind takes control, and the precelestial Five Agents transform into the posterior-heaven essence, spirit, *hun*, *po*, and intent. Their configuration is as follows:

Here, they are divided into five—essence, spirit, *hun*, *po*, and intent—without mention of qi. This is because qi enters intent, and intent is qi; thus, qi is not spoken of, but intent is. In truth, none of the five can move without qi. If intent is set aside and qi is emphasized, calling them essence, spirit, *hun*, *po*, and qi would also be acceptable.

The discriminating mind brings harm, causing us to abandon principle and follow desire, to commit wrongs and evil—all for this reason. Cultivators must construct a fortress to restrain it, keeping it still at the center so it does no harm. This is indeed a necessary task for those who practice the Dao, as the *Canon* says, "Manage and nurture the protective barriers, congeal the spirit to form the body."

As for qi, it is the beginning and end of all things. To cultivate nature, one must first cultivate qi; only by cultivating qi can life be preserved. Qi is the source of the five. At the time of utter nothingness, only qi arises first, and at the moment of attaining the Dao, it truly relies on qi. Qi is metal; only the metal of *Qian* can complete both beginning and end, which is why all alchemical scriptures speak of metal.

The so-called essence, spirit, *hun*, *po*, and intent—essence is the essence of intercourse, spirit is the spirit of thought, and intent is the intent of deluded movement, all masters of posterior-heaven emotions and desires. From this, root and dust interact, causing the fall from the original precelestial nature, while our pure, luminous, and perfect nature is obscured and vanishes without a trace. Yet in infancy, one can still preserve innate purity; once the body is broken, deliverance becomes ever more difficult.

The scripture asks, "What is the 'Yellow Path of 5,400 births'?" From the day of birth to the 5,480th day, the qi of *Qian*-metal is full, and the body is suffused with yang—this is the state of pure yang. Those of superior virtue and childlike purity, if they cultivate from this day, need not employ the work of return; they may simply sit in noble inaction. For if the vessel is unbroken, what need is there for repair? At this time of full qi, what use is there for methods of accumulating yang? Directly employing the work of refining qi into spirit is sufficient. For women, this period is 5,048 days, about a year shorter than for men, constituting a state of pure yin. Women of superior virtue, if they cultivate at this time of fullness, find it as easy as men.

Lu Ziye said, "At sixteen, a boy’s essence flows; at fourteen, a girl’s menses arrive." This is what the *Awakening to Reality* calls "the White Tiger’s first menstruation, a supreme treasure." The day when flow is about to begin but has not yet, when arrival is imminent but not yet come—this is the pure state of *Qian* and *Kun*. One day past this, the body is broken. The male is of the *Qian* body, which, when broken, becomes *Li*; the female is of the *Kun* body, which, when broken, becomes *Kan*. In men, *Kun* interacts with *Qian*, the yang line of *Qian* entering the yin hexagram, transforming *Kun* into *Kan*. True qi descends from behind the brain, passing through the spine to enter the cavity between the two kidneys, where yin and yang unite and essence is born.

In women, *Qian* interacts with *Kun*, the yin line of *Kun* entering the yang hexagram, transforming *Qian* into *Li*. The true qi of the uterus ascends, stirring the cavity between the two breasts, where yin and yang unite and menses arrive. Both arise from the fullness of spirit and qi, giving birth to the third substance—white essence and red menses. If this flow continues without return, it follows the course of human birth, and worldly affairs multiply.

Those who cultivate the Dao, if they wish to return to the root and restore the source, reversing *Li* and *Kan* back into *Qian* and *Kun*, need only employ the method of inverting *Kan* and *Li*. For men, seeking the mysterious within the *Kan* palace means extracting lead from *Kan*—the work of refining the self and laying the foundation—with the Dao residing in the cavity between the two kidneys. For women, cultivating stillness within the *Li* palace means extracting mercury from *Li*—the task of severing the Red Dragon—with the Dao residing in the cavity between the two breasts. Relying on these two cavities, one seeks the yin and yang lines and returns them to their original hexagrams, thus attaining the Dao and completing the work of inversion, restoring the unbroken state of childhood.

The *Pulse Hopes* states: "The orifices of the human body are the apertures of the hexagrams’ lines, forming the two hexagrams *Qian* and *Kun*." For example, the mouth, external genitals, and anus are single orifices, representing the three yang; the eyes, ears, and nose are double orifices, representing the three yin. The three yin and three yang of the human body—yin above and yang below—precisely form the *Earth-Heaven Peace* hexagram. Between heaven and earth lies the Great Ultimate of emptiness, which is called the "center," the place where the *Ren* and *Du* meridians intersect and where spirit and qi converge.

Based on this principle, the external correspondences of the remaining six hexagrams are as follows:

*Kan*: The ears are at the back, hence its position below. As the alchemical texts say, "Seek it in *Kan*," and "Transmit it through mouth and ear."

*Li*: When circulating the Microcosmic Orbit, the true yin of *Kan* ascends from behind and nears the eyes, while the yin fluids of *Li* descend, passing through the *Chonglou* to enter the *Dantian*. This makes it clear.

*Gen*: The *Book of Changes* says, "Stopping at the back, one does not obtain the body; walking in the courtyard, one does not see the person." *Gen* represents the *Du* meridian, rising from the *Weilü* and ending below the nose—an image of walking in the courtyard.

*Dui*: *Dui* is the mouth. As the alchemical texts say, "The union of *Dui* is not through speech." *Dui* means joy, the place where spirit and qi enter and exit.

The above pertains to the postnatal state and is used in the ascent and descent of the firing process—these are the outer eight trigrams. The inner eight trigrams correspond to the five viscera and six bowels within the human body, which cultivators of the Dao need not concern themselves with, and thus are noted but not discussed. The great function of the inner trigrams lies in the heart and kidneys, which are the *Kan* and *Li* hexagrams. Their function is taken, not their form, to be elaborated upon later.

Here, we briefly explain the positions of the pre- and postnatal eight trigrams relevant to the firing process. In the prenatal arrangement, *Qian* is south and *Kun* north, *Li* east and *Kan* west. If the four trigrams are interchanged, it becomes the postnatal arrangement, with *Li* south, *Kan* north, *Qian* east, and *Kun* west. The diagram is as follows:

East is on the left, west on the right; the left is the back, the right the abdomen. East ascends and west descends, meaning ascent from the back and descent from the front. Furthermore, the front is the yin side, the back the yang side; yang ascends from *Qian* in the east, while yin descends from *Kun* in the west.

In the postnatal arrangement, *Kun* is also in the southwest. The *Kun* hexagram has six yin lines, hence emptiness is the direction of *Kun*. The *Shuowen* says, "The southwest is called *Ao*." The *Analects* states, "Rather than flatter the *Ao*, better to flatter the stove" (see *Analects*, *Eight Rows of Dancers*). The *Ao* is the empty direction of the southwest—what use is flattery? It is also the *tang’ao* (hall’s inner chamber), where *tang* also means emptiness; it is the *mingtang* (bright hall), where *mingtang* likewise implies emptiness; it is the *xuan’ao* (mysterious chamber), the *shen’ao* (profound chamber), all signifying the abstruse and difficult to know. For *Ao* is the *Kun* direction of the southwest, the direction of emptiness. As the *Awakening to Reality* says, "To know the source of the elixir’s production, it lies only in the southwest, the native place." Alchemical texts often speak of the "*Kun* direction," alluding to the image of something arising from nothing.

In the postnatal arrangement, *Qian* is east and *Kun* west, so *Dui* is west, and the prenatal *Kan* is also west. The position of *Kun* is the same as *Dui*, and the position of *Dui* is the same as *Kan*—*Kun*, *Dui*, and *Kan* are one. In the postnatal arrangement, *Zhen* is east, and the prenatal *Li* is also east. *Qian* is the same as *Zhen*—*Qian*, *Zhen*, and *Li* are one. In the postnatal arrangement, *Kun* is also southwest, and the prenatal *Xun* is southwest. *Xun* is wind, and wind is qi; the qi of empty cavities stirs to become wind, the so-called gate of the great qi’s entry and exit—thus *Xun* is also *Kun*. In the postnatal arrangement, *Qian* retreats to the northwest, so *Gen* is also *Qian*.

The place where the human spirit and qi enter and exit is the *Niwan* Palace in the head. *Niwan* means "a pellet of mud that can be sealed," also called the ancestral aperture. The diagram is as follows:

Within the human head is an emptiness that connects to the various orifices of the ears, eyes, mouth, nose, and throat. This emptiness and its connected orifices are collectively called the *Niwan*. If distinguished, the upper part is the *Niwan*, and below the *Niwan* is called the *Mingtang*. Further below is the *Honggong* (Crimson Palace), also called the *Xuanying* (Suspended Breast), or *Xuanyong* (Suspended Obstruction). *Xuan* means suspended in emptiness; *ying* refers to the empty cavity above the chest, also called the *qiangzi* (cavity), or *xuwu qiangzi* (cavity of emptiness and nothingness), where *qiangzi* also implies emptiness.

The *Doctrine of the Mean* states: "When one attains a single good, one clings to it tenaciously in the breast." *Clinging tenaciously* signifies the act of *total retention*; *in the breast* means taking the empty space as the gateway of total retention. The character *suspended* in "suspended embryo crucible" likewise denotes *suspended in emptiness*, while the "cinnabar crucible" is so named for its redness. All cavities within the human body are red, and thus what is within the body is metaphorically called not "mercury" but "cinnabar."

The *Canticle* says: "Born before Heaven and Earth, majestic and lofty. Flanked by walls and gates, it resembles Penglai and Kunlun; encircled and sealed, its four paths are winding." This describes Penglai and the Jasper Isle, the abodes of immortals. *Majestic and lofty* speaks of its unfathomable depth, echoing the *Doctrine of the Mean*'s "the vastness of Heaven, the abyss of the deep." It is also called *Penglai*, for it depicts the primordial spirit and primordial *qi*'s native realm—supremely exalted, akin to the dwellings of immortals.

The eight vessels and nine apertures are all pervaded by *qi*, all serving as walls and gates, while the ancestral aperture of spirit and *qi* is none other than the *Niwan* Palace, which connects inner and outer. Externally, the ears, eyes, mouth, and nose; internally, the twin apertures of the *Lofty Tower*—all communicate within the emptiness of the *Niwan*. Thus, the diagram shows the interconnectedness of great and small voids. That which links them, forming the mutual exchange of spirit and *qi* between Heaven, Earth, and beings, lies precisely within these nine apertures that open to the outside. If the nine apertures are blocked, one suffocates and dies.

In the *Śūraṅgama Sūtra*, the bodhisattvas' cultivation proceeds through one of the nine apertures, or through earth, water, fire, and wind—truly, the inner and outer voids each possess the body of the Great Ultimate. The various names in the alchemical classics—*Mysterious Gate*, *Female Portal*, *Celestial Valley*, *Responsive Valley*, *Spiritual Valley*—all refer to the empty apertures. Only through emptiness can creation arise, and the void that connects inner and outer is the true center of the Mysterious Female.

The Daoists depict its form thus, and scholars should awaken to this in an instant. Hence, the *Canticle* further states: "It may be free from thought, but not from toil and sorrow. When spirit and *qi* fill the chamber, none can detain them. Those who guard it prosper; those who lose it perish. In movement and stillness, rest and activity, it ever accompanies humanity."

**Lecture Three: The Wondrous Luminosity of Inherent Nature is Possessed by All**

The Valley Spirit never dies—it returns to the Great Ultimate. At the inception of the Great Creation, white and black enfold one another like a hen’s egg. The moment of human conception is no different: within is white, without is black, white and black enfolding each other. The white is the *qi* of Prior Heaven, the true void pregnant with wondrous existence; the black is the *qi* of Posterior Heaven that arises after the union of male and female breath, wondrous existence containing the true void. The *Canticle* states: “Within the white dwells the true; square and round, a span in diameter. Intermingled, they restrain each other.” “The white is the essence of metal; the black, the foundation of water.” For the true void is a single *qi*—the essence of metal, white and issuing from *Qian*; it is also the primordial nature of *Qian*, what is called the “root of nature.” The wondrous existence is a single *qi*—the essence of water, black and issuing from *Kun*, what is called the “stem of life” of *Kun*. The white originates from Heaven and forms images in Heaven; the black emerges from Earth and takes shape on Earth. White and black enfold each other to form the shape of the Great Ultimate, no larger than a square inch, hence the *Canticle* says “square and round, a span in diameter” to describe the beginning. The inception of the embryo is no more than this.

The *Book of Changes* states: “Great indeed is the primal *qi* of *Qian*; all things owe their beginning to it” (*Qian* hexagram); “Supreme indeed is the primal *qi* of *Kun*; all things owe their birth to it” (*Kun* hexagram). The “beginning” is that first point of true yang that gives rise to the Four Images and Five Phases. The “beginning” is in Heaven, while the “birth” is on Earth—yet this is merely their image, for in truth, all lies within a single aperture. The white is the true void; the black, wondrous existence. The *Analects* says: “In painting, the plain ground precedes the colors” (*Eight Rows*). The white is the plain ground, and only the white can receive colors. The classic states: “From the One comes the Two; from the Two comes the Three; from the Three come the ten thousand things.” At the inception of human life, the *qi* of Prior Heaven is the One; the breath of father and mother is the Two. When One and Two unite to form Three, the *qi* of Prior Heaven and the *qi* of Prior Heaven within Posterior Heaven combine, and from nothing comes something—a third entity, which is the intermediate *yin*. For after conception, the umbilical cord connects to the mother’s body, and the fetus adopts the mother’s breath as its own, drawing in the external *qi* of Posterior Heaven. This *qi* of Posterior Heaven lingers with the *qi* of Prior Heaven and the *qi* of Prior Heaven within Posterior Heaven, causing the daily growth and flourishing of the form. When the form is complete, by the principle of resonance among like things, the intermediate *yin* is summoned from without—is this not the Three arising from One and Two?

Applying the theory of the Three Powers: the *qi* of Prior Heaven is Heaven; the mingled breath of father and mother is Earth; this intermediate *yin* is Man—thus the Three Powers. With the addition of the father’s essence and mother’s blood, the Five Forms are complete. Once the intermediate *yin* arrives and resides in the Yellow Spirit Chamber as the master within, the quiescent embryo stirs and moves in response. Before the intermediate *yin* enters the womb, it is without knowledge or perception, drifting through empty space; upon entering the womb, it becomes sentient and aware, for the womb contains *qi*, and the intermediate *yin* relies on it to gain consciousness.
