What has been described above is the meaning of “the fullness of the moon lies in the oral instructions.” Nowadays, those who expound the Dao are beset by too many side doors, so detailed explanation is necessary. Without deep understanding of the principle, one may stray into byways upon encountering them; with thorough knowledge, one can naturally discern them. In former times, the transmission from master to disciple relied entirely on heart-to-heart resonance and mouth-to-mouth instruction. If the master did not dissect it in detail, the disciple had to comprehend it through personal realization—how difficult it was! The subtleties of the principle are not easily clarified without explanation, yet in the past, little was expounded in depth. Even the Seven Perfected, such as Patriarch Qiu, who presided over the teachings, only spoke in broad terms, not in great detail.

The reason I explain it so thoroughly is that the Dao is a thing of great impartiality. My master, Wang, also took universal salvation as his heart, so I carry on his aspiration. Moreover, the Dao cannot be monopolized; having received this Dao, one should take the propagation of the Dao as one’s own responsibility. It is like the universal salvation of Patriarch Lü, which remains unfinished to this day, hence the opening of spirit-writing altars everywhere to spread transformation.

As for attaining the Dao, three thousand eight hundred meritorious deeds are required. Yet with a single-minded sincerity, one may also fulfill the wish—do not be daunted by difficulty. We should take benefiting others as our heart: saving one person is not as good as saving many; saving many is not as good as saving all under heaven. Only by saving all under heaven can one’s heart be somewhat fulfilled.

The upper and lower quarters combine to form the full moon; the moon’s fullness and waning are as described above. In the elixir method, the moon is also compared to the birth of yang: on the eighth day, it is half-round; on the fifteenth, fully round; on the twenty-third, half-round again; by the twenty-eighth, it returns to a crescent. The elixir method uses this to compare the waxing and waning of yang qi. The moon is also likened to the Dao-heart, with nine cycles of work, likewise taking its image from the moon.

Before one hastens to cultivate this Dao, one is like a black moon, utterly without light, akin to the dark of the moon. Through cultivation, worldly passions gradually fade, and a single speck of Dao-heart emerges—this is called the “crescent-moon furnace,” like the moon on the third day, when the first glimmer of Dao-heart appears and the furnace is established. The Pure and True Teaching also draws from the crescent moon, making it the symbol of that faith. On Three Dao Streets in Harbin, the Russians have built a Pure and True mosque, its roof bearing a crescent emblem; in Chinese Pure and True mosques, the crescent is enshrined in the central hall. The crescent moon is likened to the manifestation of the true heart, just as here it is likened to the Dao-heart. The first of the nine cycles is entirely black; the first crescent moon marks the second cycle. By the third cycle, the moonlight increases by one part to two parts, corresponding to the Dao-heart’s manifestation of two parts. In the fourth cycle, the moonlight grows further; the fifth cycle is the upper quarter, half white and half black—this is when the foundation is laid.

All nine cycles pertain to the work of refining nature; by the fifth cycle, the foundation is complete. In the sixth cycle, the moon is mostly bright; by the seventh, the darkness has nearly receded; in the eighth, only a sliver of black remains; the ninth cycle marks success, becoming a luminous full moon. The human heart gradually recedes as the white light grows; by the ninth cycle, the darkness is entirely gone, and the Dao-heart is complete—this is the “nine cauldrons with a single intent” spoken of in the *Xingming Guizhi*.

Why is it called nine? Nine is the number of yang; at the ninth cycle, one returns to pure yang. The nine-cycle elixir method draws from the moon, for by using the moon as a comparison, it is easier to understand. At the time of conception and birth, human beings are originally complete, but as knowledge unfolds and worldly desires cling, they gradually darken. When half dark and half white, it is the day of the five thousand four hundred births of the Yellow Dao. Cultivating at this point requires no laying of foundation; beyond this, the darkness increases, so one must turn black to white.

The waxing and waning of acquired spirit and original spirit, the advance and retreat of yang qi and yin qi—all can be compared to this. By sixty-four years of age, one is nearly entirely dark; when the white light is exhausted and the yang qi is spent, death follows.

The moon itself has no light; its light comes from the sun. The true yang of the prior heaven also comes from without, and only pure *kun* can obtain true yang. The black body is pure *kun*, hence it can absorb the sunlight of yang qi. If the black is slightly mixed with white, it cannot absorb. Thus, when the sun and moon conjoin, the moon absorbs the sunlight only at the dark of the moon, for the white light has receded entirely, forming a purely black body. From this, one can understand the principle of yin-yang interaction: only pure *kun* can interact with pure yang—interaction means absorption.

Upon contact, it immediately responds—thus can it absorb. After absorption, it exhales anew, cycling endlessly. This is the wondrous workings of creation, shared alike by Heaven, Earth, and humanity. Hence it is said, “The moon serves Heaven and Earth as a model for the elixir method,” and this is precisely what is meant.

Within thirty days of a month, the moon passes from darkness to a crescent, to fullness, and back to darkness—exactly thirty days in duration. Thus do calendar-makers fix thirty days as one month.

The moon is the essence of *Taiyin*; its hexagram is *Kun*. The *Kun* hexagram employs six lines. A month’s phases—new moon, full moon, first quarter, last quarter, and dark moon—pass through five stages. Five times six makes thirty, and six lines traversing five stages complete thirty days, forming one cycle. Thus does the *Cantong Qi* say, “The moon’s nodes have five-six, weaving and bearing the sun’s command.”

The moon takes the sun’s light as its own light, completing one cycle in precisely thirty days as it bears the sun’s command. When it exchanges light with the sun, both their conjunction and absorption are by the sun’s command.

Calendar-makers distinguish: the *Taiyin* calendar reckons from the moon, deriving from it; the *Taiyang* calendar reckons from the sun, and is also the Earth’s calendar. Such is their difference.

When the moon reaches the dark of the moon, it lies in the *Kun* direction—the southwest—where a black shadow appears in the *Kun* quadrant. From the moon, one may perceive the workings of Heaven and Earth. *Kun* is fundamentally black, empty, and nothing; when the moon reaches the *Kun* direction, it becomes black, empty, and nothing.

*Kan* and *Li* take over the governance of *Qian* and *Kun*: the sun acts for Heaven, the moon for Earth. *Li* (the sun) acts for *Qian* (Heaven), embodying true yang, eternally undiminished and undispersed—unchanged since the beginning of creation. The moon, however, transforms daily. Here one may discern the creative workings of *Qian*’s strength and *Kun*’s compliance.

Solar and lunar eclipses arise from irregularities in celestial qi; in elixir methods, improper firing times may likewise produce disorders of fire-heat or water-cold. Thus, when Heaven’s movements are improper, disasters arise; when human actions are unharmonious, changes occur—the principle is one and the same.

Only the sun and moon’s eclipses can be predicted in advance; though firing-time disasters cannot be foreknown, they may be detected from subtle signs. All arise from imbalance of yin and yang—there is no difference between the Way of Heaven and the Way of humanity.

In the human element, the firing time requires the balance of two eights. In elixir methods, this is likened to “half a catty and eight taels”—half a catty and eight taels being the same. It is also compared to the waxing and waning crescents: when the body reaches the waxing crescent, the heart reaches the waning crescent. Dividing body and heart into upper and lower crescents, the yin and yang on both sides must be evenly regulated.

At the waxing crescent, advance the yang fire to *mao*; at the waning crescent, retreat the yin tally to *you*. The upper and lower crescents—half a catty and eight taels—unite to form the elixir, that is, the union of yin and yang to complete the Dao. Only when true yin and true yang are evenly balanced can they conjoin; otherwise, they cannot.

This is also called “the union of dragon and tiger.” *Mao* Wood belongs to the Azure Dragon of the East; *you* Metal belongs to the White Tiger of the West. *Mao* and *you* face each other across the Central Palace, thus they unite—this is the union of dragon and tiger. The *Cantong Qi* says, “The dragon calls to the tiger; the tiger absorbs the dragon’s essence.” The addition of “calling” and “absorbing” clarifies their relationship—it is the union of upper and lower crescents.

The *Book of Changes* takes *Zhen* as the dragon and *Dui* as the tiger; the union of dragon and tiger is thus the union of *Zhen* and *Dui*. The original heart is *Li*, while the body is *Kan*—this is the union of *Kan* and *Li*.

Because *zi*, *wu*, *mao*, and *you* share the same locus, the union of *zi* and *wu* is called the union of *Kan* and *Li*, while the union of *mao* and *you* is called the union of *Zhen* and *Dui*. Their function occurs in the Central Palace. Elixir texts name this “harmonizing the four images and gathering the five phases.” *Zi*, *wu*, *mao*, and *you* correspond to the four hexagrams *Kan*, *Li*, *Zhen*, and *Dui*.

Yang above and yin below, the union of *Kan* and *Li* is the union of *Zhen* and *Dui*—for *zi*, *wu*, *mao*, and *you* converge in the *Kun* Palace and there unite. To clarify this, a diagram is provided as follows: from the beginning straight to the Central Palace is the union of *zi* and *wu*, yet its locus is the gate of *mao* and *you*—thus it may also be called the union of *mao* and *you*. From this, one may understand clearly.

It is also said, “gathering the five phases”—this is the same, with the addition of the Central Palace, which becomes the five phases. *Zi*, *wu*, *mao*, and *you* represent Water, Fire, Wood, and Metal; adding the true Earth of the Central Palace completes the five phases.

*Zi*, *wu*, *mao*, and *you* converge in one place: the union of *zi* and *wu* is the union of *mao* and *you*; the union of *mao* and *you* is the pairing of Wood and Metal; the union of *zi* and *wu* is the union of Water and Fire. The distinction lies only in inner and outer—Wood and Metal are outer, *zi* and *wu* inner.

As for the precise division of inner and outer, and the method of their union, these will be detailed when discussing the firing times of the microcosmic orbit.

When cultivating the Dao and practicing the work of returning to emptiness, upon reaching the time when yang arises, one should naturally know the heart-transmission of the timely *zi* and the oral instructions of the full moon. At this point, one may proceed to the work of nine returns and seven reversions.

*Direct Exposition of the Celestial Mechanism, Scroll Four, Lecture Fourteen*

Gradual and sudden methods, the Human and Celestial Origins—
nine layers in sequence, a single intent giving rise to the body.

When cultivating the Dao and practicing the work of returning to emptiness, upon reaching the time when yang arises, one should naturally understand the heart-transmission of the timely *zi* and the oral instructions of the full moon, only then may one apply the work of nine returns and seven reversions. These principles have already been expounded in detail in the previous two lectures.

Now, let us further examine the nine-layered heart-refining practice of Master Li Hanxu, expounding it in full. Through this, the entirety of Daoist cultivation may be broadly grasped.

First, we present Master Li’s original text, followed by a detailed exposition.

His work is titled *The Scripture of Nine-Layered Heart Refinement in the Great Dao of the Human Origin*, also known as *The Nine-Layered Heart-Refining Daoist Discourse*:

**First Layer: Refining the Impure Heart**
This is the refinement of the heart that is not yet pure. The impure heart is filled with delusive thoughts and wandering musings. Delusive thoughts arise from greed and desire, while wandering musings stem from unawareness. When practitioners sit in meditation, though they may wish to cast aside worldly concerns, no sooner have delusive thoughts been dispelled than wandering musings arise anew. The method lies in "cessation and insight," through which these may gradually be dissolved.

To cease is to fix the mind behind the navel hall and before the Gate of Life. Slightly below this, there is a realm of emptiness and nothingness. The heart is stilled here, and inwardly observed. The heart illumines the void, guarding the qi, bound within the compass of the square and circle, moving between their bounds. With each breath, it returns to the root, merging with the natural workings of creation. Immovable and majestic, it establishes the primordial foundation of purity. From this, a single thread of heart-light connects with a wisp of true qi, blending in profound harmony, tranquil and at ease. This is the initial work of refining the heart and nurturing the qi.

The practice of refining the heart in Daoist cultivation is divided into nine stages, each to be discussed separately. It is called the "Great Dao of the Human Origin" because the elixir method distinguishes between the Human Origin and the Celestial Origin. The so-called "Great Elixir of the Celestial Origin" also begins with the Human Origin, for the Human Origin harmonizes with the Celestial Origin. The Celestial Origin pertains entirely to the primordial Dao, culminating in the return to emptiness. The Human Origin, however, begins with later-heaven methods of effort and action. In ancient times, many advanced from the Human Origin to the Celestial Origin, for the Human Origin is the method of laying the foundation and replenishing the root. Those of superior virtue and wisdom may directly cultivate the Celestial Origin, but for duller roots, beginning with the Human Origin is easier. The Celestial Origin is a method of sudden and complete cultivation, while the Human Origin is gradual, as the saying goes: "The Dao perfects the form; the art prolongs life."

Master Li’s nine-layered method was personally transmitted by the Patriarch Lü, and it is a superior and simple practice.

**First Layer: Refining the Impure Heart**
This is the refinement of the self, beginning with the later-heaven body and mind. The later-heaven heart is filled with delusive thoughts and wandering musings. Delusive thoughts are simply thoughts. Wandering musings arise without prior intention, stirring within without purpose, drifting aimlessly, appearing and vanishing unpredictably. Wandering musings arise from nothing, sometimes present and sometimes absent, while thoughts are focused and arise from specific imaginings. Thus, thoughts may be forcibly restrained and overcome, but wandering musings cannot be controlled. For example, poverty giving rise to thoughts of wealth is a delusive thought, born of desire. Wandering musings, however, arise suddenly in the mind regardless of whether one is thinking or not, arriving without cause and thus difficult to prevent beforehand.

The method for refining these two lies in cessation and insight. Cessation is the stilling of thoughts; insight is the observation of the mind. Cessation and insight are practiced in quiescence, in stilling the mind at the utmost good. Fixing the mind of utmost good at the Gate of the Mysterious Female is "dual cultivation of cessation and insight," a term from Buddhism. Daoism calls it "dual cultivation of nature and life" or "dual cultivation of the wondrous aperture."

In Buddhism, the dual cultivation of cessation and insight has many levels. Initially, there is the "Lesser Cessation and Insight," followed by the "Mahayana Cessation and Insight," and finally the "Heavenly and Human Cessation and Insight." The Lesser Cessation and Insight is a gradual method; the Mahayana Cessation and Insight is a method of sudden and complete cultivation; the Heavenly and Human Cessation and Insight pertains to the final return to emptiness, a matter of advanced practice rather than initial work. Here, insight is the observation of emptiness to still thoughts. As stated in the *Lesser Cessation and Insight*: "Cessation is fixing the mind on a condition." That condition is emptiness. One may fix the mind between the eyebrows, or below the navel. Fixing the mind is observing where it is fixed, which is cessation. The empty, thoughtless heart is placed in one of these three locations.

These three locations correspond to three layers. Fixing the mind between the eyebrows aligns with the method of the Tongshanshe. However, fixing the mind between the eyebrows requires withdrawing inward by one *cun*, meaning it remains in the realm of emptiness. Fixing the mind below the navel also requires distancing it from the flesh by one *cun* and three *fen*.

Between the eyebrows is where the light of nature manifests. Thus, the Tathāgata emits the white light of the *ūrṇā* between the eyebrows—this is the luminosity inherent in one’s original nature. The moment when "the empty chamber generates brightness" is when light emanates between the eyebrows, for the space between the eyebrows is the empty chamber.

One *cun* and three *fen* below the navel is the locus of fetal breathing, where the true breath resides. As Liao Chanxuan said: "Before the navel wheel, behind the kidneys, there is a true golden tripod." The golden tripod is the coagulation of the true breath, which practitioners will naturally recognize when the time comes. One *cun* and three *fen* below the navel lies a sphere of true qi, revolving like a wheel—this is the root of life. After birth, the root of life remains here, and as the infant grows, the fetal breath disperses, leaving this place as an empty cavity.

Those who cultivate *xing* (nature) alone begin at the aperture between the eyebrows; those who cultivate *ming* (life) alone begin at the locus below the navel. As Ancestor Lü said: *"To cultivate nature without cultivating life is to remain a yin spirit for ten thousand kalpas, scarcely able to enter sagehood"*—such a one can only become a ghost-immortal of the yin realm. *"To cultivate life without cultivating nature is to share the longevity of heaven and earth as a fool."* (See *The Song of Knocking on the Trigrams*, with slight textual variations.) Thus, one must cultivate both nature and life together. In dual cultivation, one must begin at the "margin’s center."

The *margin* denotes the boundary; the center of this boundary is the empty aperture where inner and outer voids converge—this is the central empty aperture within the microcosm of the human body. As this is the root of respiration and the gateway through which the heart-spirit enters and exits, both spirit and qi gather here. To practice the Dao, one must first unite and interdependently bind the heart-spirit and breath. This is precisely where one should begin.

Now, spirit pertains to nature, while qi pertains to life. Humans rely on qi for life and on spirit for consciousness. These two—spirit and qi—are humanity’s most precious treasures. Qi is acquired from without, stolen from heaven, earth, and the myriad things, yet only through spirit can qi be drawn into the body. Thus, when a person dies and the spirit scatters, qi no longer enters. There are two kinds of death: if the spirit scatters first, the dying person becomes unconscious at the end, exhaling without inhaling, and expires when the breath is fully spent. If the qi is severed first, followed by the scattering of the spirit, the person remains lucid at the moment of death, suddenly ceasing to breathe, and even after death, the eyes may remain clear for some time.

If either spirit or qi departs the body, death is certain. Therefore, one must preserve both spirit and qi to sustain life. Cultivating the Dao is cultivating these two—spirit and qi. Cultivating nature begins with spirit; cultivating life begins with qi. For dual cultivation, one must begin where spirit and qi unite. Neither the space between the eyebrows nor the locus below the navel is appropriate. Only the "margin’s center" aperture, through which spirit and qi enter and exit, is suitable. Beginning dual cultivation from this aperture encompasses all subtle apertures, which is why the Three Teachings all symbolize it with the character *zhong* (center).

Yet this is the *empty* center, not the *true* center. Only when spirit and qi unite and the heart and breath interdependently bind does the true center arise. As Bai Yuchan said: *"Where the thought moves is the Mysterious Female."* Thus, this is called the "margin’s center." The margin’s center is where the true center arises; Daoists call it the "round center" or the "suspended center."

*"Focusing the mind on the margin’s center"* is what Daoists call *"dual cultivation of the subtle aperture,"* Confucians call *"dual cultivation of nature and life,"* and Buddhists call *"dual cultivation of śamatha and vipaśyanā."* The Great Vehicle’s śamatha-vipaśyanā is practiced naturally and effortlessly, proceeding with ease. The lesser śamatha-vipaśyanā is the practice of knowing where to rest. The Great Master Sima of Nanyue specialized in teaching the Great Vehicle’s śamatha-vipaśyanā, which first requires emptying and purifying the heart while nurturing qi. Without śamatha-vipaśyanā, one naturally aligns with it—this is the sudden method. For those of us practicing both sudden and gradual methods, beginning by focusing the mind on the margin’s center is without error. This is the work of the Heavenly Origin.

Li Xian described the initial stage of the Human Origin’s work: *"It lies behind the navel hall and before the Gate of Life. Slightly below these is a circle of emptiness. The mind rests here, and one inwardly observes it."* This is the method of focusing the mind below the navel, a technique for prolonging life through artifice, hence called the Human Origin. The reason it is termed the *"Great Dao of the Human Origin"* and differs from the Heavenly Origin lies in its reliance on intention to generate the subtle aperture.

The method involves first using the qi of postnatal breathing, drawing it deeply inward to gather below the navel, forming this circle of emptiness, and then observing it with the heart. Thus, it is said: *"The heart illumines the void within"* (that is, one *cun* and three *fen* below the navel, separated from the flesh). This is the initial practice. When the breath reaches this point, the heart also rests here. With the heart and breath interdependently bound, primordial chaos arises, and creation unfolds.

First cultivating life and then uniting it with nature—nature is bestowed by heaven, while life is established by humans—hence it is called the Human Origin. The method requires first regulating the breath: on the inhalation, direct it with intention to the inner Golden Tripod; on the exhalation, guide it with intention to the outer locus below the navel. Once the primordial qi below the navel is activated, unite the spirit with the breath, ascending to rest at the margin’s center and descending to settle below the navel.

The square pertains to earth; the round pertains to heaven. The round aperture connects with heavenly qi; the square aperture connects with earthly qi. *"Within the square and circle"* is the center between heaven and earth; *"between the compass and square"* is the true Golden Tripod one *cun* and three *fen* below the navel. Once the primordial qi below the navel is generated and the compass’s center is formed, the true intention moves between inner and outer to maintain it.

Those over sixty-four years of age or in poor health should practice this method to preserve life. The nine layers of heart refinement begin with the Human Origin and ascend to the Heavenly Origin, progressing from the upper-grade elixir method to the supreme vehicle—this is the path. Through the interdependence of heart and breath, the heart unites with the breath, and true breath is established. The former *"circle of emptiness"* congeals into the subtle aperture, which is the prenatal within the postnatal. Then, uniting the two hearts, primordial chaos enters the prenatal.

When cultivation reaches this point, the initial stage of heart refinement is complete.

But this so-called *intention* remains the state between intentional and unintentional—if one forces it excessively, it will instead stir deviant fire and lead to illness. Beware.

The second layer of heart refinement is the refinement of the heart in *ding* (meditative absorption). Previously, a thread of heart-light connected with a wisp of true *qi*; if one could penetrate directly into the profound obscurity, one would naturally break through the subtle aperture. Yet because the stabilized heart is not firm, it is often swayed by the *shen* of discriminating consciousness. Heart and *qi* separate, and one still cannot perceive the original face. The method lies in the moment when heart and breath interdepend: extinguish all awareness, so that the heart abides within *qi* without knowing it, and *qi* envelops the heart without its realizing—vaporous and intermingled, fused into one. This is the work of refining the heart to unite with *qi*. The second layer, refining the heart in *ding*, means the heart is stabilized within *qi*. It remains within the *"circle of emptiness"*—this is stabilization in oneness. With long and thorough practice, one naturally forgets through stabilization, returning to primordial chaos, unaware and unknowing, inwardly forgetting the heart and outwardly forgetting the body, and the subtle aperture naturally emerges.

Zhang Sanfeng said: *"The subtle aperture comes and goes without fixed location."* He also said: *"The entire path of the Yellow Court is the subtle aperture."* The so-called *"path of the Yellow Court"* refers to the domain of breathing. The *qi* of inhalation and exhalation enters and exits through the mouth and nose; wherever the breath can reach is the *"path of the Yellow Court."* Here, based on the location of the *dantian*, we clarify the scope of this *"path"* and illustrate it as follows:

**Scope of the Path of the Yellow Court**
*Upper, Middle, and Lower Fields*
- *External:* Crown, Center (navel), Perineum (Yin Heel)
- *Internal:* Celestial Valley, Responding Valley, Spirit Valley
- *Corresponding Points:* Mud Pill Palace, Crimson Palace, Valley Passage

From the crown to the center is the Upper Field; from the center to the navel is the Middle Field; from the navel to the perineum is the Lower Field. The *dantian* within the body only becomes a *dantian* once the inner elixir is formed—without the elixir, there can be no *dantian*. It is like farmland: what is planted in the field determines its name. If grass is planted, it is grassland; only when wheat is planted does it become wheat field. Only when the elixir is present does it become a *dantian*; without the elixir, there is no *dantian*—only the empty aperture of the *dantian*’s location. In truth, the *dantian*’s location is merely the *"path of the Yellow Court."*

The entire *"path of the Yellow Court"* is the subtle aperture, so the subtle aperture has distinctions of upper and lower, as well as inner and outer. It may appear above or below, with no fixed abode. When it appears above, it is the upper subtle aperture; when below, the lower subtle aperture. Its form is like a ring, its whiteness like snow, its softness like silk. Whether circular (○) or crescent-shaped ( ), these refer to the outer subtle aperture. As for the inner subtle aperture, it is the elixir’s origin—what the Buddha called the ever-turning *Dharmachakra*. When the elixir’s origin first forms, it is the size of a soybean, constantly pulsing within the Lower Field. In moments of deep stillness, one can perceive it.

When we begin practice, the subtle aperture that appears is the outer subtle aperture. The inner subtle aperture can only be seen when the Three Origins merge, the elixir’s origin congeals, and true breath is established. The subtle aperture is the most secret aperture, and it has never been openly explained. Now, for the benefit of later learners, it is explained in detail.

Once the heart is stabilized within the *"circle of emptiness"* below the navel, a thread of luminous heart connects with a wisp of true breath, naturally entering profound obscurity. From this obscurity arises a state of vagueness, and the subtle aperture emerges—this is the manifestation of the outer subtle aperture. However, because the stabilized heart is not firm, the subtle aperture is not easily seen at once. One must first return to emptiness, extinguishing all awareness, so that heart and breath interdepend, spirit and *qi* unite. From stabilization to forgetting, entering primordial chaos, one can then perceive it. This so-called entry into primordial chaos is the work of returning to emptiness.

For us, the work of returning to emptiness is a single direct step, but for others, it involves three stages. The mass of *qi* below the navel is the treasure of life. First, the heart stabilizes and enters it. Second, heart and breath interdepend, spirit and *qi* unite. Third, one gradually enters profound obscurity, returning to the state of emptiness. Though slightly different from our method, after returning to emptiness, the attainment of the medicine is the same.

The third layer of heart refinement is the refinement of the *"returning"* heart. Previously, vaporous and intermingled, fused into one, the return of heavy *yin* is called the heart of Heaven and Earth—this is the subtle aperture. At this moment, essence, *qi*, and spirit all reside in the prenatal. The primordial chaos has just divided, and true essence, true *qi*, and true spirit are not yet distinct. If one can keep the heart utterly unmoving, one may immediately gather and circulate it. Yet, confronted with sights never before seen and sounds never before heard, with wondrous scenes before one, one is at a loss, and the heart stirs, falling into the postnatal—then essence, *qi*, and spirit separate.

The method lies in the moment the subtle aperture first appears: immediately tread upon the fire-cloud, advance to the *weilu* (tailbone), firm the heart, soften the breath, strike the iron drum to pass the Three Passes, and rest at *Kunlun* (the head). This is the work of refining the heart to advance *qi*. The third layer, refining the *"returning"* heart, is the time of the seven-day return, when the first *yang* arises—this is the fire-timing of *yang*’s birth. Beneath heavy *yin*, a single *yang* returns. As true *yang* gradually fills, the subtle aperture appears, and one has reached the state of vagueness. Once the subtle aperture manifests and essence, *qi*, and spirit unite without separation, if there are no stray thoughts, one may gather it.

Upon witnessing what was never seen before and hearing what was never heard before, one may generate a heart of astonishment and joy, or thoughts of doubt and fear—immediately reverting to the postnatal state, where essence, *qi*, and spirit stand divided as three. At this stage of the human element, with deliberate action and effort, the method lies in the moment the subtle aperture first appears: do not cling to any form, but continue the work of settling the spirit externally, with an unmoving heart. After a while, when *yang* *qi* is abundant, gently apply intention to guide it to the *weilu* (tailbone).

The fire-cloud is none other than *yang* *qi*. When the first *yang* arrives at the tailbone, it has reached the body. Why not say "body" but "tailbone"? Because within the *yinqiao* point lies the prenatal true *yang*, of the same kind as the externally incoming true *yang*, thus able to summon and gather the external *yang*. As the external *yang* approaches, it first arrives at the tailbone; internal and external unite, reaching the *mingmen* (Life Gate), and the external kidneys rise—this is the *living midnight*; then it surges to the heart’s palace, and one becomes aware of the external kidneys’ rise—this is the *living noon*. After this awareness, one must immediately apply stillness. From this, the second *yang* and third *yang* follow, and *yang* *qi* fills to abundance, naturally ascending from the tailbone to the *niguan* (mud pill).

At this stage of the human element, fearing attachment to form may give rise to the heart and cause one to miss the opportunity, one first uses subtle intention to guide it upward, breaking through the tailbone to pass the Three Passes, thereby opening the postnatal pathway. In the celestial element, one allows it to proceed naturally; once the subtle aperture opens, all apertures in the body naturally open without exception. Here, the human element employs intention first, differing from the celestial element.

The *living midnight* refers to the arising of *yang*; the *living noon*, to awareness. For those of us with postnatal, broken bodies, *yin* *qi* is abundant, and the initial arrival of *yang* is barely perceptible—only a slight twitching on the skin is felt. In truth, *yang* *qi* has already ascended to the crown. The practice of firming the heart and softening the breath is none other than the work of *ding* (settling) and *wang* (forgetting).

The fourth layer refines the heart of retreat and concealment. Previously, treading the fire-cloud and passing the Three Passes, the heart and *qi* followed, entering the *niguan* (mud pill). Yet within the *niguan* palace, if the consciousness-spirit stirs, *qi* chills and congeals, unable to transform into true water to sprinkle and irrigate the Three Palaces—all prior effort is lost. The method lies in the crown of *Kunlun*: still the heart and master quietude, merging with *qi*; *qi* then transforms into sweet liquid, descending from the upper palate. Curl the tongue to receive the dew, swallow and send it down, directing the heart to the *jiangong* (crimson palace), to the *huangting* (yellow court), to the *yuanhai* (primordial sea)—a resonant sound follows all the way to the base, and the subtle aperture’s manifestation reappears. This is the work of refining the heart to obtain *qi*.

The fourth layer refines the heart of retreat and concealment, corresponding to the sevenfold return within the body. The *yang* of the *yinqiao* draws in external *yang*; as external *yang* arrives, it stirs the *mingmen* and the kidneys rise. I respond with *ding* and *wang* externally; *yang* *qi* then surges upward to the heart’s palace, and I remain aware of the external kidneys’ rise, still applying *ding* and *wang* externally. *Yang* can thus reach the crown—this is the internal path of *yang* *qi*. In the celestial element’s elixir method, one allows natural ascent and descent; what I perceive is only a tingling numbness on the body—initially like fleas jumping, then spreading into a full-body tingling. One must immediately apply the *wang* (forgetting) practice; only then can *yang* *qi* transform into liquid, descending from *Kunlun*, penetrating the heart with cool clarity. At this moment, the heart’s joy is beyond words.

In the human element, with deliberate effort at every step, when *qi* ascends, one quietly abides in the *niguan*, focusing attention for a long while, then guiding it downward, receiving it with the palate and swallowing it past the *chonglou* (throat tower). Again, direct attention to guide it down to the *jiangong*, *huangting*, and back to the *yuanhai*—this is the microcosmic orbit of the sevenfold return. At this point, one should cease the fire; if continued further, the body will grow uncomfortable, and the *qi* will scatter.

The heart and kidneys interact, water and fire mutually aiding; *yang* *qi* ascends, cool liquid descends, with a sound like thunder reaching the base. The ascent is *yang* rising to meet *yin*; the descent is *yin* descending to meet *yang*—this is the work of the microcosmic orbit’s river chariot.

The fifth layer refines the heart of foundation-building. Previously, entering the *niguan* and returning to the *qi* point, the river chariot’s path has been established. Proceeding with a single heart day and night without rest, how could the foundation not be complete within a hundred days? Yet if there is laxity, desire, or intermittent practice, the elixir foundation will not solidify. Foundation-building gathers essence and unites spirit; if effort is not diligent, spirit remains scattered—how can one prolong life?

Those who uphold the Daoist method must practice according to the *zi-wu* (midnight-noon) cycle, daily drawing and adding, extracting *kan* (Water) to fill *li* (Fire), accumulating gold to solidify the abdomen. This is the work of refining the heart to accumulate *qi*.

The fifth layer refines the heart of foundation-building. If the prior work is practiced without negligence, after three hundred microcosmic orbits, the foundation is successfully built. Yet if practice is intermittent, effort not diligent, or the heart unsettled by external distractions, or if the method is not followed correctly, even with great diligence, no gold will accumulate, and progress remains difficult. Foundation-building means establishing and solidifying the elixir foundation. If one is careless and idle, how can daily progress be made and permanence achieved? Thus, the Dao lies in gathering essence and uniting spirit, daily renewing. Those who lack diligence must reform to become diligent; those whose practice is incorrect must correct it to conform to the method.

To achieve one microcosmic orbit is to realize its corresponding effect. Through daily refinement and accumulation, filling the abdomen with gold, the three hundred orbits will naturally be completed with success. In human cultivation, many begin with diligence but end in laxity. By applying corrective effort and self-discipline, one can avoid repeating past mistakes and gradually attain accomplishment. This work of refining the heart and accumulating *qi* is most essential and must not be neglected.

The sixth layer refines the heart of nature. Previously, with the river chariot in motion and the gathering of essence to unite spirit, the numinous root is filled. From this, heart-fluid descends while kidney-*qi* ascends—this is the union of Kan and Li. In profound stillness, a sign arises: vast as the tide, half water-*qi*; misty as fog, half cloud-*qi*. This is called the initial stirring of gold and water, the stage of refining the jade-fluid returning elixir. Yet if the heart is not single-minded, the task of fully realizing nature remains unaccomplished. The method lies in the day when gold and water first arise: from the cinnabar field, they descend to the bubbling spring, instantly converging at the tailbone. Regulating the true breath, one stirs and dances it, causing it to surge upward to the celestial valley, then trickle down to be swallowed into the yellow court. Thus, with daily irrigation, the heart-ground becomes cool and clear, blood transforms into cream, intent congeals into earth, and within earth, mercury is born. Mercury’s nature is round and luminous, unchanging before phenomena—like a spirit-sword in hand. Mencius said, “To fully realize one’s heart is to know one’s nature.” The immortals call this “yin elixir” or “inner elixir.” This is the work of refining the heart to clarify nature.

The sixth layer refines the heart of nature, which is the work of refining the self to generate true intent. In the Heavenly Origin, refining the self is the initial practice. When true intent is achieved, it regulates the firing times, allowing one side to follow nature. In the Human Origin, one first guides *qi* with personal intent—this intent is not true. Only after foundation-building does one undertake this work of refining the self, so that true intent forms and true breath stands firm. This pertains to the work of the character *xing* (nature). Previously, heart and kidneys interacted: kidney-*qi* ascended, heart-fluid descended. The ascending is the true fire within Kan, yang uniting with yin; the descending is the true water within Li, yin uniting with yang. Internally, heart and kidneys unite; externally, gold and water naturally merge, producing a mass of true intent, misty and boundless, circulating through the mysterious pass, gathering without dispersing. The two earths form a jade tablet—this is the external aspect. Internally, heart and kidneys unite, water and fire mutually assist, and after three hundred orbits are completed, a mass of true breath naturally arises—this is the elixir origin, pulsing day and night. From below the navel, it ascends via the heel vessel and returns without cease. Sealed with intent, it rests below the navel, revolving like a wheel. It naturally opens and closes, and the true breath rises and falls, reaching the crown above and the heels below, circulating throughout. At this time, one applies the work of warming and nurturing the elixir origin. Only the two words “stabilize” and “forget” are used: daily, one forgets for a time, stabilizes for a time, and rests for a time. In all six periods, work must be balanced with stabilization and forgetting. After a year of warming and nurturing, the elixir origin transforms into the returning elixir, and externally, a sign appears—a black sphere before the eyes. Still, one stabilizes and forgets, and gradually the black sphere turns red. This is the attainment of the inner elixir and the completion of nature, preparing for the great seven-day orbit of the macrocosm.

The seventh layer refines the already clarified heart. Previously, the river chariot of gold and water was called “inner refinement” by the immortals. Here, there is also the work of external refinement, where external aligns with internal, and the true heart gathers without dispersing. Though the inner body is clarified, mercury’s nature is prone to flight; though inner cultivation is achieved, the yin elixir is easily corrupted. If preservation is impure, the heart-nature may perish again. The method lies in blending the empty and luminous heart with the wondrously existent nature, mixing cinnabar with earth and planting it in the other’s domain. The other’s domain is empty, so I fill it; the other is without, so I provide. Casting the existent into the nonexistent, the solid into the void, the heart dies and does not move. In an instant, the primordial *qi* arrives from the formless. The first hour is one yang, like *Zhen*; the second hour is two yang, like *Dui*. At the second hour, it is time to conjoin the elixir. From the other side, a strand of true *qi* emerges—metaphorically, the tiger born from water; from this side, a speck of mysterious light descends—metaphorically, the dragon emerging from fire. The two, dragon and tiger, meet, and nature and emotion interact in a great battle. Like heaven and earth in darkness, body and heart become still. Suddenly, three yangs stir, like the *Qian* hexagram. Like tide, like fire; like mist, like smoke; like lightning, like thunder; like snow, like blossoms. Within the body, yang *Qian* shines brilliantly. I wield the sword, grasp the seal, step the *gang* and pace the *dou*, stirring the primordial harmony. With fierce firing and extreme refinement, it pierces the three passes and ascends to the mud pill. Every pore in the body opens, unlike the previous jade-fluid river chariot. Swallowing and ingesting it, the primordial controls the acquired, and nature and life unite as one—this is the great return. Nature belongs to fire, its number seven; life belongs to metal, its number nine. Returning to the origin, it is called the seven-return, nine-cycle golden-fluid great elixir. From this, lead comes to restrain mercury, and the heart remains ever luminous, mercury unshaken. This is the work of refining the heart to preserve spirit.

The seventh layer refines the already clarified nature, which is the work of refining *qi* to transform spirit.

Refining the already clarified nature means using one’s own empty numinosity to commune with the heavens’ and earth’s empty numinosity. The heart rests entirely within the void, and thus one must augment forgetfulness and diminish fixation. Forgetfulness is the forgetting of both body and mind. One’s body and mind dissolve into the void, becoming no different from emptiness, and from this emptiness arises creation, revealing the great celestial revolution’s visions. The black orb transforms into a red orb, also called the "crimson tangerine"—this is the moment of "refining the elixir within fire." The red orb circles the body, now rising, now falling, ascending from behind and descending from the front, looping around back and front, divisible into the *zi-wu-mao-you* positions. At these four cardinal points, the orb’s movement must slow slightly; beyond them, it suddenly soars to the highest peak or plunges to the lowest depths, like a fox refining the elixir—others see only the red orb’s rise and fall.

These *zi-wu-mao-you* positions lie entirely outside the body; that realm is the void itself, and one’s true intention fills the void. As for what occurs within the body: *"White clouds gather at the crown, sweet dew sprinkles Mount Sumeru."* The red orb ascends, and hot *qi* rises with it. Soon the red orb descends, and the sweet dew likewise falls, resounding like thunder. After seven days, the red orb transforms into a purple mist enveloping the body. At this time, yin demons surge forth like tides and flames—this is the vision of passing the great celestial revolution, the moment in *Journey to the West* when crossing the Flaming Mountains. During this passage, past karmic deeds manifest, and the ten thousand demons converge. All one’s greed, anger, delusion, and attachment, along with karmic burdens from past lives, appear before the eyes; every person ever glimpsed likewise emerges in vision.

The "grasping the sword and wielding the seal" refers to the sword of wisdom, which is the true awakened heart—one must use this true heart to subdue all, wielding it like a sword to sever everything. The seal is the celestial seal, the heart of heaven. When yin demons surge like tides, the slightest movement of the heart topples the elixir crucible. Thus one must grasp the sword and wield the seal to subdue all, resting the heart in boundless emptiness without allowing a single thought to arise.

The *gang* are the four cardinal directions—*zi, wu, mao, you*; the *dou* is the Dipper’s handle, the fixed pivot. "At this time, one must stir the primordial harmony with fierce firing and extreme refinement"—this is the crossing of the Flaming Mountains in *Journey to the West*. The mountain spans eight hundred *li*, with no path through, and within it gather ten thousand demons, flames raging like a furnace. Only after passing this trial does one attain peace: every pore in the body opens like popping beans, both itchy and hot, leaving one as if drunk or dazed, blood and *qi* reversing their flow throughout the body. After a while, a cool fluid descends, and the whole body becomes refreshed.

The reason one must use the Plantain Fan to cross the Flaming Mountains is that the plantain is a leaf of wood, soft though wooden in nature, likened to the fluid of wood. Fanning generates wind, and wind is the true yin *qi*. This *qi* reaches the mouth and transforms into a most refreshing liquid, though before reaching the mouth, it remains gaseous. Three times the Plantain Fan is wielded to fan the wind and extinguish the fire—three represents *qian*, metal; the plantain is wood, thus metal and wood unite.

When Sun Wukong meets Princess Iron Fan, their tender words symbolize the meeting of true yin and true yang, their harmonious union. The fire of the Flaming Mountains is the fire of the discriminating mind; the Bull Demon King is the great white ox of Snow Mountain, representing *kun* earth, the earth of intention. Intention harbors many delusions—dispelling delusion reveals truth. Intention is inherently continuous, hence "beheading it only causes another head to grow." Only the Bull Demon King embodies delusive intention, and its fire must be quelled with yin softness, extinguishing delusion to return to truth—this is the illumination of the heart and seeing of nature. The Bull King’s submission to righteousness relies on the encirclement of vajra warriors, symbolizing the body pervaded by *qian* metal.

The seven emotions and six desires of human life are all delusive intentions; at this time, truth and delusion wage war, yin and yang clash. Having passed the great celestial revolution, delusion reverts to truth, turbid yin is exhausted, and true yang returns to the body, forming a purely yang physique. Thus it is called the "seven-return, nine-cycle golden-fluid great return elixir," distinct from the lesser celestial revolution’s jade-fluid return elixir. The lesser revolution is the seven-return; the greater revolution is the nine-cycle. If referring to either alone, both lesser and greater revolutions involve seven-return and nine-cycle.

After passing the great celestial revolution, the heart remains unmoving, merging with the great void—henceforth begins the work of spirit departure. The eighth layer refines the heart, having already subdued it, to enable communion with the spirit. Prior to this, the seven-return and nine-cycle used lead to restrain mercury, and the heart was settled. Yet it must be warmed and nurtured, so that the body’s *qi* fully transforms into spirit, and the body’s spirit can roam beyond.

Thus, taking the twelve months of the year’s qi and climate, excluding the third and ninth months for bathing, the remaining ten months are for advancing and retreating—hence the name "ten-month nurturing." This does not mean ten months of effort are required; otherwise, though the heart may be settled, it will not be numinous. Refine and forge it, and the numinous heart will manifest day by day. When numinous, it moves; when it moves, it transforms; when it transforms, it transcends—thus the work of spirit departure arises, and one is no longer deluded by worldly emotions. This is the practice of refining the heart into spirit.

The eighth layer refines the already subdued heart to enable communion with the spirit—this is precisely the work of spirit departure. After obtaining the external elixir, one must employ the nurturing practice, which takes approximately one year. Excluding the third and ninth months for bathing, ten months remain—this is the "ten-month gestation." The method involves connecting the void within one’s body to the void of heaven and earth. Over time, the purple radiance enveloping the body transforms into golden light, which gradually expands to the size of a chariot wheel, covering the crown of the head—this is the vision of spirit departure. At this stage, one is often unaware, for the mind is lost in forgetfulness, neither knowing nor perceiving. It is fitting to have a companion to guard, protect, and rouse one, so that upon awakening, the spirit departs at once.

Initially, the spirit is immature and cannot travel far, stopping after five or ten paces. With gradual refinement, it travels farther, eventually reaching thousands or tens of thousands of miles. At this point, one looks back upon the physical body as dung and dirt, and many at this stage achieve liberation through the corpse, dissolving away. Moreover, from this point onward, the refinement of spirit into void is a matter of the spirit alone—even without the physical body, cultivation remains possible, so there is no harm in relinquishing it. Yet even if relinquished, the physical body may endure for a long time without decay.

The ninth layer refines the already numinous heart to return it to emptiness. Through deep nurturing, the spirit has departed without confusion, following the heart’s desires without hindrance, treading upon clouds and mist, roaming the islands of the sea—what joy is this! But if the numinous heart is not empty, it cannot contain the ten thousand existences; thus, there is the practice of refining emptiness. In refining emptiness, the heart and breast are vast and boundless, all existences become nothing, and a single qi of pure emptiness spirals between heaven and earth—this is I, yet not I; this is emptiness, yet not emptiness. When the world is destroyed, only emptiness remains undestroyed; when heaven and earth are obstructed, only emptiness is unobstructed. Thus, the spirit fills the void, and the Dharma pervades the realms of sand. This is the beginning and end of heart refinement—nothing surpasses it.

The ninth layer refines the already numinous heart to return to emptiness. The numinous spirit must be swept clean, shattered into emptiness, becoming a thousand, ten thousand, or a hundred million emanation bodies—then the transformations of spiritual power are boundless. At this stage, the spirit has shed its womb, so it may return to emptiness as spirit alone, or return to emptiness while retaining the physical form. Everywhere in the void is where my spirit arrives; everywhere in the void is my Dharma body. Thus, the ninth layer of heart refinement is accomplished.

This chapter begins with the initial steps and concludes with the return to emptiness, for it first addresses the work of connecting life, which differs slightly in practice. After entering the great celestial revolution, it is no different from the primordial Dao now discussed. The Human-Origin Elixir method takes one’s intention as primary, embodying the meaning of "intent generating the body." The method lies in unifying intention to reach sincerity. However, if one’s cultivation is not yet mature, the firing times may not be easily mastered, and its simplicity does not compare to the Heavenly Origin. The ancients said that only those of the highest capacity can cultivate the Heavenly Origin; those of middling endowment must progress from the Human Origin to the Heavenly Origin.

**Fifteenth Lecture: The Governing Vessel lies behind, the Conception Vessel lies before.**

When the work of returning to emptiness reaches the moment when yang arises in the body, one may proceed to the practice of the Microcosmic Orbit. The initial arising of yang is the *living zi hour*; our awareness of yang’s arising is the *living wu hour*. Within the Microcosmic Orbit, there are seven internal returns and nine external reversions: internally, water and fire intermingle; externally, metal and wood unite. The alchemical texts caution against attachment to the physical form—this is a necessary mindfulness in our practice, though in truth the work is performed upon the body. If the firing times are appropriate, then internally, Kan and Li merge, achieving the harmony of water and fire; externally, Zhen and Dui unite, achieving the fusion of metal and wood. The harmony of water and fire is the union of heart and kidney, though the alchemical texts avoid the term “union of heart and kidney” to prevent attachment to the body. In reality, even when called the union of heart and kidney, it does not refer to the physical form but to the intermingling of true yang and true yin in the postnatal state. Externally, it is the union of true yang and true yin in emptiness—this is the Reverted Elixir of Jade Liquid. Though the Microcosmic Orbit has the image of the River Chariot, one cannot clearly perceive it due to the heaviness of yin in our bodies; in the Macrocosmic Orbit, the River Chariot becomes perceptible.

The path of the River Chariot is none other than the Governing and Conception Vessels: the Governing Vessel lies behind, the Conception Vessel lies before, with the Governing Vessel as yang and the Conception Vessel as yin. Since ancient times, few have been willing to explain these two vessels in detail; here, I shall expound upon them thoroughly:

The Great Ultimate gives rise to Heaven and Earth, and Heaven and Earth are one Great Ultimate; likewise, each human body also contains a Great Ultimate. The Great Ultimate has three points of intersection, and the human body also has three points of intersection; from these three points arise the three barriers. The three points of intersection in our bodies are the three points where the Governing and Conception Vessels meet.

The Governing Vessel runs along the back of the body, the Conception Vessel along the front, and between them lies a vertical vessel called the *Chong* (Thoroughfare Vessel) and a horizontal vessel called the *Dai* (Belt Vessel). Both the Chong and Dai Vessels connect with the Governing and Conception Vessels, serving as their subsidiary channels. Here, I illustrate this with a diagram:

From conception to birth, I have already roughly explained once. Now, I shall discuss the Governing and Conception Vessels again: after the union of male and female essence, yang revives on the seventh day, and the primordial embryo is established. After another forty-nine days, the Governing Vessel first forms, originating at the *weilu* (coccyx). The *weilu* lies behind the anus, where the tailbone is. Slightly above the *weilu*, two white points appear—these are the two kidneys of the *mingmen* (Gate of Life). The vessel extends straight up to the head, reaching its end at two openings—the nostrils. Slightly above these, two black points form—the eyes. This is the Governing Vessel, the master of the body’s formation. After some days, the Conception Vessel forms along the front of the body, connecting internally from the upper and lower lips of the mouth to the Governing Vessel, descending to the *yinqiao* point in the lower region, where it again meets the Governing Vessel.

The upper portion of the Governing Vessel enters internally from the upper lip, curves around the ears to the spine, intersecting with it; slightly below, it turns inward to the *chonglou* (throat), reaching the lower lip to connect with the upper end of the Conception Vessel. The lower portion of the Governing Vessel branches off at the anus, surging into the abdomen to reach the navel—this is the Belt Vessel. From the anus, it descends straight to the *yinqiao* orifice, where it meets the Conception and Thoroughfare Vessels. The Thoroughfare Vessel rises from the *yinqiao* straight up to the *chonglou*; thus, the *yinqiao* orifice is a three-way intersection, for the Conception, Governing, and Thoroughfare Vessels all converge here.

The middle portion of the Governing Vessel extends from the spine’s great bone, branching into two vessels that reach the backs of the hands, and from the spine’s great bone, two vessels enter the backs of the feet. The Conception Vessel is similar, branching from the front to the palms of the hands and from the front to the soles of the feet. These Governing and Conception Vessels contain no blood vessels; they are the pathways for the opening and closing of prenatal true breath. In the postnatal state, they become obstructed and impassable.

Humans possess eight vessels: the Conception, Governing, Thoroughfare, and Belt Vessels, as well as the Yang Linking, Yin Linking, Yang Heel, and Yin Heel Vessels. The qi of the Orbit ascends from the *weilu* and *yinqiao* to the upper body, then turns into the hands and feet, circulating through the Governing and Conception Vessels—thus, the arising of yang is first sensed in the hands and feet. As the *Book of Changes* states: *“The yellow center penetrates the pattern, beauty resides within, and flows into the four limbs.”* This is precisely the case.

The Great Ultimate has three points of intersection—upper, middle, and lower—and the Governing and Conception Vessels also have three points of intersection. The upper intersection at the back is where the spine’s great bone crosses in a cross shape; at the front, it is where the upper and lower lips meet at the center of yin and yang. The lower intersection is the cross-shaped meeting at the *yinqiao*—all connected by the Belt Vessel.

At birth, humans first develop the eight vessels, then the viscera, and finally the bones and flesh; the eight vessels and nine meridians all encircle and support the Central Palace. In the postnatal state, the Governing and Conception Vessels become obstructed and impassable, and we rely on the nine reversions and seven returns to open them. Opening these two vessels is thus called “unlocking the barriers and expanding the orifices.”

The Governing Vessel is the path of yang’s ascent, the Conception Vessel the path of yin’s descent; through the Governing and Conception Vessels, the Orbit is circulated—this is essential for the Macrocosmic Orbit. In the Microcosmic Orbit, however, the ascent occurs via the Thoroughfare Vessel, and one need not rely on the Governing and Conception Vessels to circulate it.

The Governing Vessel pertains to the body, the Conception Vessel to the heart—thus the terms “body” and “heart” arise. In the postnatal state, the Governing Vessel is obstructed and impassable; what substitutes for it in performing its function is the spine.

The spine courses through the entire body, thus the function of the Governing Vessel remains. The Microcosmic Orbit operates through the "midnight-noon ebb and flow," extracting lead to replenish mercury. Lead is the yang within Kan (Water), while mercury is the yin within Li (Fire); extracting and replenishing is termed "midnight-noon ebb and flow." The pathway it traverses is the Thoroughfare Vessel, which courses through midnight and noon. When external yang arises at the Yin Heel Vessel, it stimulates the Gate of Life, causing the external kidneys to ascend. As it ascends via the Thoroughfare Vessel, it arouses awareness, thus activating the noon hour. Once the yang has ascended and can be stabilized through forgetting, a cool fluid descends to the Gate of Life, and the yang retracts. The circulation of yang qi is entirely conducted by the Thoroughfare Vessel, for at this time, true breath has yet to be established, the Conception and Governing Vessels remain obstructed, and the pathways of ascent and descent are naturally unknown.

Midnight, noon, dawn, and dusk are the four cardinal palaces, corresponding to the nine reversions and seven returns, eight returns and six residences: the nine reversions occur at midnight, the seven returns at noon, the eight returns at dawn, and the six residences at dusk. Why is "six residences" placed at dusk? Because of the metal within water. The nine reversions return the yang of the ninefold celestial number; the seven returns revert the yin of the sevenfold celestial number—returning the celestial nine’s yang and reverting the celestial seven’s yin. The eight returns signify emotions returning to nature, where nature is the celestial three and terrestrial eight of the eastern direction. Six represents water; terrestrial six is water, which is born in the ninth earthly branch (Shen) and bathed in the tenth (You)—hence "six residences." In the postnatal state, Qian (Heaven) and Kun (Earth) transform into Kan (Water) and Li (Fire); the true emotions within Kun ascend to become Li. Now, true emotions return to their original position in Kun—thus the terms "eight returns" and "six residences." Nine and seven, eight and six—these are precisely metal and wood conjoined, water and fire intermingled. Six (water) and nine (metal) make fifteen; eight (wood) and seven (fire) make fifteen—hence the terms "metal within water" and "wood within fire."

In the diagram above, midnight, noon, dawn, and dusk may be added: dawn and dusk lie within the circle of the Girdle Vessel, midnight at the Yin Heel Vessel, and noon at the crown—this is what is meant by "within the cavity." When the work of the Microcosmic Orbit reaches the state of forgetting through stabilization, one enters a profound obscurity, becoming a formless, utterly Kun-like body. From this formless void, yang is born. When yang arises in the emptiness before reaching the body, one remains in a state of undifferentiated obscurity. Upon sensing it in the body, one transitions from profound obscurity to a state of vague perception—externally, there are signs; internally, there are visions. Suddenly, a white light appears, and when this white light reaches the body, this is an external sign. Yang first arrives at the four limbs, producing a keen sensation—one feels a tingling numbness in the limbs, another external sign. At this moment, one must stabilize externally, which is termed "congealing the spirit within the qi cavity." As the saying goes: *"To become a Buddha or an immortal requires no effort—only congeal the spirit within the qi cavity."*

At this time, one senses within the mysterious emptiness a mass of misty, swirling qi gently coalescing. The heart now perceives that yang has arisen, for this awareness arises from the stirring of yang qi. If the spirit lingers within the body, the yang qi will dissipate; thus, one must stabilize within the void, congealing the spirit into the misty qi. At this point, heart and breath are interdependent, yet one must still congeal the spirit, for the spirit has been aroused to awareness, and there is a risk of its dispersion. Therefore, one must congeal the spirit into the qi, stabilizing it within the mysterious aperture—one cannot be negligent. A slight, subtle intention must still be employed, hence the term "martial fire," referring to the use of this subtle intention. Since the yang is newly born, without martial fire, there is a risk that awareness will cause the spirit to scatter, or that arising thoughts will cool the fire. Thus, one must employ a subtle intention, using martial fire for intense refinement—this is the explanation from the perspective of practice. From the perspective of obtaining the medicine, it is a matter of fire driving metal to move; only by driving it with fire does the metal ascend—this is achieved by fixing true intention within the aperture.

As yang qi grows increasingly abundant, one feels a tingling numbness throughout the body; the eighty-four thousand pores all sense the arising of yang. The eighty-four thousand hairs of Sun Wukong can all transform because yang has reached the pores. When the entire body tingles, the alchemical texts speak of the "steaming fire phase": initially, it reaches the body but does not enter within. Once the tingling is felt, it has entered within, and a method is needed to retain it in the body—this lies in forgetting. If one cannot forget the body and instead attends to it, the yang will depart. Only by forgetting can it be retained—this is of utmost importance. By retaining the yang qi and accumulating it daily, yin qi naturally recedes. When half of it has receded, the spirit enters the qi cavity and naturally stabilizes in the most perfect place. If yang is sufficiently abundant, one can naturally stabilize and forget the body—this is the transition from effort to ease.

Once the practice reaches the state of effortless stabilization and forgetting, the awareness becomes spiritual awareness, distinct from the previous use of the acquired spirit. Formerly, the acquired spirit was in control, necessitating forgetting; now, the acquired spirit has receded, and the original spirit is numinous, naturally able to stabilize and forget. There is no need to cease the fire—simply forgetting serves to cease it. When employing subtle intention, stabilization is martial fire, and forgetting is civil fire; cessation of practice is the cessation of fire. Upon reaching the state of ease, the fire phase may shift: stabilization becomes civil fire, and forgetting becomes the cessation of fire. Intentional stabilization is martial fire; natural stabilization is civil fire; forgetting both body and heart is the cessation of fire—these are the distinctions.

At this point, one may continue the work. During the phase of effort, cessation of practice serves to cease the fire.

When in a state of naturalness, forgetting serves to cease the fire. Day by day, one abides in primordial chaos; day by day, yang is born. Only when it is full and sufficient can this state be attained. At this point, stabilization becomes the act of gathering, and forgetting becomes sealing and securing—unlike the earlier stage, when stabilization was for refinement and forgetting for gathering, while cessation of practice was for sealing.

As Lü Zu said: *"Do not idly guard the furnace and watch the fire—simply settle the spirit and rest in naturalness."* This is the state of ease and spontaneity. Here, yang naturally becomes full and sufficient; there is no need for refinement—merely stabilization to gather and forgetting to seal will suffice. Only at this stage can true reversion and restoration occur. When the original spirit is numinous and capable of awareness, the small celestial cycle begins to take effect.

Previously, during the phase of effort, yang would rise and be perceived, and upon perception, one would stabilize. Yet this single act of perception already introduced impurities, falling into the postnatal and lacking purity—it was not the unadulterated prenatal. Only when one reaches the state of self-stabilization and self-forgetting does it become purely prenatal, allowing for the extraction of one *kan* to fill *li*. During the phase of postnatal admixture, though gathering occurs, it is not pure and thus lacks efficacy. Only when spiritual awareness is complete and gathering is thorough—after three hundred celestial cycles—does the foundation-laying effect manifest.

In the earlier phase of effort, the awareness of yang’s arising was accompanied by intention; it could not be the purest source of water, for it was slightly entangled with the forms of body and heart. This could supplement the postnatal but not enter the prenatal; it could nourish the body but not form the elixir. When yang arose and was perceived, and then gradually receded after perception, this was all due to the acquired spirit’s activity. Only when awareness arises from the spirit, and sealing is also from the spirit—all occurring naturally—does it belong to the prenatal.

Upon attaining spiritual awareness, a tingling numbness signals yang’s arising, though initially unnoticed. Once arisen, it reaches the lively *wu* hour; stabilization and forgetting remain external, and yang naturally recedes. When the practice becomes deeply familiar, cool fluid descends, penetrating the heart with a refreshing chill—like emerging from a bath, the body is utterly at ease. This marks the completion of one celestial cycle. Because daily immersion in primordial chaos has accumulated sufficient yang, when yang arrives, it stirs the yin heel vessel and harmonizes with the original *qi*. The Gate of Life is the inner kidney, connected to the outer kidney; when yang reaches the Gate of Life, the outer kidney rises.

Simultaneously, yang *qi* ascends through the thoroughfare vessel into the crown, stirring awareness. Awareness is the spirit. Once yang’s arising is spiritually perceived, stabilization and forgetting remain external as one enters the *qi* cavity. After a short while, the yang organ retracts, and the wooden fluid descends—this fluid, transformed from *qi*, flows from the crown down to the elixir field. This cool fluid is most precious, suffusing the body with refreshing coolness and filling the heart with indescribable joy. Where once there was chaos, now there is clarity.

In this phase, the fire and spiritual awareness harmonize naturally. The pores first tingle with numbness, then ease; as the cool fluid descends, the itching ceases—here, one celestial cycle is complete. The numinous fluid atop the crown is true yin, also called jade fluid. When outer yang and inner yang converge and surge upward, inner yang is the yang within *kan*—the true fire of the Gate of Life. *Kan* is water, yet it conceals true fire. Surging upward to the *li* palace—*li* is fire, yet it conceals true water. Fire comes to meet water, and the true water within *li* descends. The outer kidney rises with the ascent of fire and retracts with the descent of water. True water flows into the Gate of Life—water comes to meet fire, both being the intermingling of water and fire.

The true fire within *kan* ascends—this is extracting *kan* to fill *li*. The true water within *li* descends—this is returning *li* to *kan*. *Kan* and *li* intermingle, restoring the body of *qian* and *kun*. The Gate of Life, the inner kidney, conceals true fire and governs the body, thus being the body’s yang. Awareness resides in the brain as the heart; the heart conceals true water and is yin. Thus, in the comparison of the physical form, the intermingling of water and fire is the intermingling of the *qi* of heart and kidney. This is the natural lively *zi* hour and lively *wu* hour—the natural union. With prolonged practice, one can reverse aging: white hair turns black, fallen teeth regrow.

This internal union is also called the union of *kan* and *li*, dragon and tiger. There is also an external union—the union of *qian* and *kun*, *zi* and *wu*. At the lively *zi* hour, external yang arrives at the mysterious cavity of the central palace, which connects to the yin of respiration. Once it reaches the mysterious cavity, it swiftly communicates within. As the *qi* of the Gate of Life surges into the heart, it becomes the lively *wu* hour; spiritual awareness naturally emerges from stabilization within the mysterious cavity, piercing through primordial chaos to reveal light.

The spirit of spiritual awareness emerges and, upon condensation, enters the *qi* cavity to unite with the incoming external yang—this is the union of metal and wood. The union occurs within the mysterious cavity. Yin is originally wood mercury, concealed within *li*, while the incoming *qi* is lead—lead being metal. This is the union of *qian* and *kun*, *zi* and *wu*. The phenomena within the body include only tingling numbness and the movement of the yang organ. The descent of yin and ascent of yang go unnoticed; only the movement of the yang organ is perceived. The descending cool fluid, originally transformed from true *qi*, becomes seminal essence through the union of spirit and *qi*—this is the prenatal within the postnatal. The entire body tingles with numbness, itching permeating every pore—this completes one celestial cycle. At this point, one celestial cycle is concluded.

The union of *qian* and *kun*, *zi* and *wu*, is the ninefold return—returning the yang of emptiness. The union of *kan* and *li*, dragon and tiger, is the sevenfold reversion—retreating the yin within the body. The ninefold return advances yang; the sevenfold reversion retreats yin—these are their distinctions.

When the natural spiritual awareness arises, it is the primal spirit taking charge—only then does it accord with the method. During forced practice, though yang may rise, it cannot unite, for the water source is not clear, and the body cannot be pervaded by tingling softness. Only when the water source is utterly pure does it avail the work. In sleep, when utmost stillness is reached, stillness gives rise to yang; though the water source is inherently clear, if spirit and *qi* do not unite, yang may rise yet remain unperceived. If yang rises in sleep and one awakens, waking is itself awareness. But once this awareness occurs, should worldly desires or stray thoughts intrude, the water source becomes impure, and the elixir cannot form.

Formerly, the Ming Prince Ji received the Dao from his master, then met Master Wu again. Wu asked, “What method did your previous master teach you?” Prince Ji replied, “He instructed me to wait until sleep, then upon waking to yang’s rise, to apply effort in gathering and refining. Yet after long practice, I saw no effect—why?” Wu told him, “When you wake and become aware of yang’s rise, then rise to sit in meditation, you have already attached to the form of the body. This impure water source—how can the elixir form?” From this, we know the water source must be clear. Without first completing the work of returning to emptiness, achieving stillness of body and mind, yang cannot arise. When yang does arise, it requires various firing times for the water source to remain clear and unmuddied.

The alchemical texts’ “striking bamboo to summon the turtle” refers to the living *zi* hour; “playing the zither to beckon the phoenix” refers to the living *wu* hour. When yang arises in sleep, if natural spiritual awareness is reached and the primal spirit is alert, the work is already complete without waking, and one celestial cycle is accomplished. There is also the martial fire of the water clock, where the clock’s marking is the counting of breaths. But the counting must be done by listening with the ear—not by mentally noting the number, but by the breath naturally reaching the ear so it may be heard.

Exoteric and heterodox schools misconstrue the firing times, giving rise to endless complications. Thus, they speak of counting breaths or prolonging them, unaware that there exists a natural, true firing time that requires no kindling herbs or burning rushes. When one reaches a state of effortless spontaneity, the primal spirit acts on its own, without need for deliberate exertion.

At the outset of practice, from yang’s rise to its retraction may take, for example, a quarter-hour. Gradually, this shortens—from a quarter-hour to ten minutes, then five, and at its swiftest, to one minute. From *zi* to *hai*, a single cycle takes but a minute—this is the stage of mastery. Continuing without interruption, it is said, “The free-flowing river chariot turns hundreds of times.” Each movement and stillness follows in unbroken succession. After three hundred cycles, the minor celestial orbit is complete, and the elixir foundation is laid.

The elixir foundation lies one *cun* and three *fen* below the navel. At first, it pulses up and down—descending to the Gate of Life, ascending to the Heart Palace. The eyes should be fixed upon this point one *cun* and three *fen* below the navel to seal and stabilize it. As the *Yinfu Jing* says, “The mechanism lies in the eyes”—this is precisely it. The *Xingming Guizhi* states, “Heart and kidneys are separated by eight *cun* and four *fen*, hollow as a lotus root yet interconnected”—this is the same principle. Focusing here for three to five days, the pulsation at one *cun* and three *fen* below the navel forms a circle. True breathing is established, naturally opening and closing.

When the sevenfold reversion and ninefold return reach one cycle per minute, continue for three hundred celestial orbits—then the minor orbit is complete, and one may return to the body of youthful purity, the foundation successfully laid.
